Next: <a href="#Keeping-it-Consistent" accesskey="n" rel="next">Keeping it Consistent</a>, Previous: <a href="#Commenting-on-your-Journal" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Commenting on your Journal</a>, Up: <a href="#Keeping-a-Journal" accesskey="u" rel="up">Keeping a Journal</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Currency-and-Commodities-1">4.5 Currency and Commodities</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-currency"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-commodity"></a>

<p>Ledger is agnostic when it comes to how you value your accounts.
Dollars, Euros, Pounds, Francs, Shares etc. are all just &ldquo;commodities&rdquo;.
Holdings in stocks, bonds, mutual funds and other financial
instruments can be labeled using whatever is convenient for you (stock
ticker symbols are suggested for publicly traded assets).<a class="footnote" id="DOCF3" href="#FOOT3"><sup>3</sup></a>
</p>
<p>For the rest of this manual, we will only use the word &ldquo;commodities&rdquo;
when referring to the units on a transaction value.
</p>
<p>This is fundamentally different than many common accounting packages,
which assume the same currency throughout all of your accounts.  This
means if you typically operate in Euros, but travel to the US and have
some expenses, you would have to do the currency conversion
<em class="emph">before</em> you made the entry into your financial system.  With
ledger this is not required.  In the same journal you can have entries
in any or all commodities you actually hold.  You can use the
reporting capabilities to convert all commodities to a single
commodity for reporting purposes without ever changing the underlying
entry.
</p>
<p>For example, the following entries reflect transactions made for a
business trip to Europe from the US:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2011/09/23 Cash in Munich
    Assets:Cash                               â¬50.00
    Assets:Checking                          $-66.00

2011/09/24 Dinner in Munich
    Expenses:Business:Travel                  â¬35.00
    Assets:Cash
</pre></div>

<p>This says that $66.00 came out of checking and turned into 50
Euros.  The implied exchange rate was $1.32.  Then 35.00 Euros were
spent on Dinner in Munich.
</p>
<p>Running a ledger balance report shows:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f example.dat bal
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">             $-66.00
              â¬15.00  Assets
              â¬15.00    Cash
             $-66.00    Checking
              â¬35.00  Expenses:Business:Travel
--------------------
             $-66.00
              â¬50.00
</pre></div>

<p>The top two lines show my current assets as $-66.00 in checking (in
this very short example I didn&rsquo;t establish opening an opening balance
for the checking account) and â¬15.00.  After spending on dinner I have
â¬15.00 in my wallet.  The bottom line balances to zero, but is shown
in two lines since we haven&rsquo;t told ledger to convert commodities.
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Naming-Commodities" accesskey="1">Naming Commodities</a></li>
<li><a href="#Buying-and-Selling-Stock" accesskey="2">Buying and Selling Stock</a></li>
<li><a href="#Fixing-Lot-Prices" accesskey="3">Fixing Lot Prices</a></li>
<li><a href="#Complete-control-over-commodity-pricing" accesskey="4">Complete control over commodity pricing</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Naming-Commodities">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Buying-and-Selling-Stock" accesskey="n" rel="next">Buying and Selling Stock</a>, Previous: <a href="#Currency-and-Commodities" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Currency and Commodities</a>, Up: <a href="#Currency-and-Commodities" accesskey="u" rel="up">Currency and Commodities</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Naming-Commodities-1">4.5.1 Naming Commodities</h4>

<p>Commodity names can have any character, including white-space.
However, if you include white-space or numeric characters, the
commodity name must be enclosed in double quotes &lsquo;<samp class="samp">&quot;</samp>&rsquo;:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">1999/06/09 ! Achat
    Actif:SG PEE STK         49.957 &quot;Arcancia Ãquilibre 454&quot;
    Actif:SG PEE STK      $-234.90

2000/12/08 ! Achat
    Actif:SG PEE STK        215.796 &quot;Arcancia Ãquilibre 455&quot;
    Actif:SG PEE STK    $-10742.54
</pre></div>

<p>Please note that, for querying quoted commodities, the quotes need to be escaped, as follows:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f d reg -l 'commodity == &quot;\&quot;Arcancia Ãquilibre 454\&quot;&quot;'
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Buying-and-Selling-Stock">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Fixing-Lot-Prices" accesskey="n" rel="next">Fixing Lot Prices</a>, Previous: <a href="#Naming-Commodities" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Naming Commodities</a>, Up: <a href="#Currency-and-Commodities" accesskey="u" rel="up">Currency and Commodities</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Buying-and-Selling-Stock-1">4.5.2 Buying and Selling Stock</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-buying-stock"></a>

<p>Buying stock is a typical example that many will use that involves
multiple commodities in the same transaction.  The type of the share
(AAPL for Apple Inc.) and the share purchase price in the currency
unit you made the purchase in ($ for AAPL).  Yes, the typical
convention is as follows:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2004/05/01 Stock purchase
    Assets:Broker                     50 AAPL @ $30.00
    Expenses:Broker:Commissions        $19.95
    Assets:Broker                  $-1,519.95
</pre></div>

<p>This assumes you have a brokerage account that is capable of managing
both liquid and commodity assets.  Now, on the day of the sale:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2005/08/01 Stock sale
    Assets:Broker                    -50 AAPL {$30.00} @ $50.00
    Expenses:Broker:Commissions        $19.95
    Income:Capital Gains           $-1,000.00
    Assets:Broker                   $2,480.05
</pre></div>

<p>You can, of course, elide the amount of the last posting.  It is there
for clarity&rsquo;s sake.
</p>
<p>The &lsquo;<samp class="samp">{$30.00}</samp>&rsquo; is a lot price.  You can also use a lot date,
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">[2004/05/01]</samp>&rsquo;, or both, in case you have several lots of the
same price/date and your taxation model is based on
longest-held-first.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Fixing-Lot-Prices">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Complete-control-over-commodity-pricing" accesskey="n" rel="next">Complete control over commodity pricing</a>, Previous: <a href="#Buying-and-Selling-Stock" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Buying and Selling Stock</a>, Up: <a href="#Currency-and-Commodities" accesskey="u" rel="up">Currency and Commodities</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Fixing-Lot-Prices-1">4.5.3 Fixing Lot Prices</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-fixing-lot-prices"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-consumable-commodity-pricing"></a>

<p>Commodities that you keep in order to sell at a later time have
a variable value that fluctuates with the market prices.  Commodities
that you consume should not fluctuate in value, but stay at the lot
price they were purchased at.  As an extension of &ldquo;lot pricing&rdquo;, you
can fix the per-unit price of a commodity.
</p>
<p>For example, say you buy 10 gallons of gas at $1.20.  In future
&ldquo;value&rdquo; reports, you don&rsquo;t want these gallons reported in terms of
today&rsquo;s price, but rather the price when you bought it.  At the same
time, you also want other kinds of commodities&mdash;like stocks&mdash;
reported in terms of today&rsquo;s price.
</p>
<p>This is supported as follows:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2009/01/01 Shell
    Expenses:Gasoline             11 GAL {=$2.299}
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>This transaction actually introduces a new commodity, &lsquo;<samp class="samp">GAL
{=$2.29}</samp>&rsquo;, whose market value disregards any future changes in the
price of gasoline.
</p>
<p>If you do not want price fixing, you can specify this same transaction
in one of two ways, both equivalent (note the lack of the equal sign
compared to the transaction above):
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2009/01/01 Shell
    Expenses:Gasoline             11 GAL {$2.299}
    Assets:Checking

2009/01/01 Shell
    Expenses:Gasoline             11 GAL @ $2.299
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>There is no difference in meaning between these two forms.  Why do
both exist, you ask?  To support things like this:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2009/01/01 Shell
    Expenses:Gasoline             11 GAL {=$2.299} @ $2.30
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>This transaction says that you bought 11 gallons priced at $2.299 per
gallon at a <em class="emph">cost to you</em> of $2.30 per gallon.  Ledger
auto-generates a balance posting in this case to Equity:Capital Losses
to reflect the 1.1 cent difference, which is then balanced by
Assets:Checking because its amount is null.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Complete-control-over-commodity-pricing">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Fixing-Lot-Prices" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Fixing Lot Prices</a>, Up: <a href="#Currency-and-Commodities" accesskey="u" rel="up">Currency and Commodities</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Complete-control-over-commodity-pricing-1">4.5.4 Complete control over commodity pricing</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dmarket-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dexchange-_0022COMMODITY-_005b_002c-COMMODITY_002c-_002e_002e_002e_005d_0022"></a>

<p>Ledger allows you to have very detailed control over how your
commodities are valued.  You can fine tune the results given using the
<samp class="option">--market</samp> or <samp class="option">--exchange <var class="var">COMMODITY</var></samp> options.  There
are now several points of interception; you can specify the valuation
method:
</p>
<ol class="enumerate">
<li> on a commodity itself,
</li><li> on a posting, via metadata (effect is largely the same as #1),
</li><li> on an xact, which then applies to all postings in that xact,
</li><li> on any posting via an automated transaction,
</li><li> on a per-account basis,
</li><li> on a per-commodity basis,
</li><li> by changing the journal default of <code class="code">market</code>.
</li></ol>

<p>Fixated pricing (such as &lsquo;<samp class="samp">{=$20}</samp>&rsquo;) still plays a role in this
scheme.  As far as valuation goes, it&rsquo;s shorthand for writing
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">((s,d,t -&gt; market($20,d,t)))</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>A valuation function receives three arguments:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">source</code></dt>
<dd><p>A string identifying the commodity whose price is being asked for
(example: &lsquo;<samp class="samp">EUR</samp>&rsquo;).
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">date</code></dt>
<dd><p>The reference date the price should be relative.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">target</code></dt>
<dd><p>A string identifying the &ldquo;target&rdquo; commodity, or the commodity the
returned price should be in.  This argument is null if <samp class="option">--market</samp>
was used instead of <samp class="option">--exchange <var class="var">COMMODITY</var></samp>.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>The valuation function should return an amount.  If you&rsquo;ve written
your function in Python, you can return something like
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">Amount(&quot;$100&quot;)</samp>&rsquo;.  If the function returns an explicit value,
that value is always used, regardless of the commodity, the date, or
the desired target commodity.  For example,
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">define myfunc_seven(s, d, t) = 7 EUR
</pre></div>

<p>In order to specify a fixed price, but still valuate that price into
the target commodity, use something like this:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">define myfunc_five(s, d, t) = market(5 EUR, d, t)
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">value</code> directive sets the valuation used for all commodities
used in the rest of the data stream.  This is the fallback, if nothing
more specific is found.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">value myfunc_seven
</pre></div>

<p>You can set a specific valuation function on a per-commodity basis.
Instead of defining a function, you can also pass a lambda.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">commodity $
    value s, d, t -&gt; 6 EUR
</pre></div>

<p>Each account can also provide a default valuation function for any
commodities transferred to that account.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">account Expenses:Food5
    value myfunc_five
</pre></div>

<p>The metadata field &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Value</samp>&rsquo;, if found, overrides the valuation
function on a transaction-wide or per-posting basis.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">= @XACT and Food
    ; Value:: 8 EUR
    (Equity)                     $1

= @POST and Dining
    (Expenses:Food9)             $1
        ; Value:: 9 EUR
</pre></div>

<p>Lastly, you can specify the valuation function/value for any specific
amount using the &lsquo;<samp class="samp">(( ))</samp>&rsquo; commodity annotation.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2012-03-02 KFC
    Expenses:Food2               $1 ((2 EUR))
    Assets:Cash2

2012-03-03 KFC
    Expenses:Food3               $1
        ; Value:: 3 EUR
    Assets:Cash3

2012-03-04 KFC
    ; Value:: 4 EUR
    Expenses:Food4               $1
    Assets:Cash4

2012-03-05 KFC
    Expenses:Food5               $1
    Assets:Cash5

2012-03-06 KFC
    Expenses:Food6               $1
    Assets:Cash6

2012-03-07 KFC
    Expenses:Food7                1 CAD
    Assets:Cash7

2012-03-08 XACT
    Expenses:Food8               $1
    Assets:Cash8

2012-03-09 POST
    Expenses:Dining9             $1
    Assets:Cash9
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger reg -V food
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">12-Mar-02 KFC                   Expenses:Food2                2 EUR        2 EUR
12-Mar-03 KFC                   Expenses:Food3                3 EUR        5 EUR
12-Mar-04 KFC                   Expenses:Food4                4 EUR        9 EUR
12-Mar-05 KFC                   Expenses:Food5                   $1           $1
                                                                           9 EUR
12-Mar-06 KFC                   Expenses:Food6                   $1           $2
                                                                           9 EUR
12-Mar-07 KFC                   Expenses:Food7                1 CAD           $2
                                                                           1 CAD
                                                                           9 EUR
12-Mar-08 XACT                  Expenses:Food8                   $1           $3
                                                                           1 CAD
                                                                           9 EUR
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Keeping-it-Consistent">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Journal-Format" accesskey="n" rel="next">Journal Format</a>, Previous: <a href="#Currency-and-Commodities" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Currency and Commodities</a>, Up: <a href="#Keeping-a-Journal" accesskey="u" rel="up">Keeping a Journal</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Keeping-it-Consistent-1">4.6 Keeping it Consistent</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dstrict"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-accounts"></a>

<p>Sometimes Ledger&rsquo;s flexibility can lead to difficulties.  Using a
freeform text editor to enter transactions makes it easy to keep the
data, but also easy to enter accounts or payees inconsistently or with
spelling errors.
</p>
<p>In order to combat inconsistency you can define allowable accounts and
payees.  For simplicity, create a separate text file and define accounts
and payees like
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">account Expenses
account Expenses:Utilities
</pre></div>

<p>Using the <samp class="option">--strict</samp> option will cause Ledger to complain if any
accounts are not previously defined:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger bal --strict
Warning: &quot;FinanceData/Master.dat&quot;, line 6: Unknown account 'Liabilities:Tithe Owed'
Warning: &quot;FinanceData/Master.dat&quot;, line 8: Unknown account 'Liabilities:Tithe Owed'
Warning: &quot;FinanceData/Master.dat&quot;, line 15: Unknown account 'Allocation:Equities:Domestic'
</pre></div>

<p>If you have a large Ledger register already created use the
<code class="command">accounts</code> command to get started:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger accounts &gt;&gt; Accounts.dat
</pre></div>

<p>You will have to edit this file to add the <code class="code">account</code> directive in
front of every line.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Journal-Format">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Converting-from-other-formats" accesskey="n" rel="next">Converting from other formats</a>, Previous: <a href="#Keeping-it-Consistent" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Keeping it Consistent</a>, Up: <a href="#Keeping-a-Journal" accesskey="u" rel="up">Keeping a Journal</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Journal-Format-1">4.7 Journal Format</h3>

<p>The ledger file format is quite simple, but also very flexible.  It
supports many options, though typically the user can ignore most of
them.  They are summarized below.
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Transactions-and-Comments" accesskey="1">Transactions and Comments</a></li>
<li><a href="#Command-Directives" accesskey="2">Command Directives</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Transactions-and-Comments">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Command-Directives" accesskey="n" rel="next">Command Directives</a>, Previous: <a href="#Journal-Format" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Journal Format</a>, Up: <a href="#Journal-Format" accesskey="u" rel="up">Journal Format</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Transactions-and-Comments-1">4.7.1 Transactions and Comments</h4>

<p>The initial character of each line determines what the line means, and
how it should be interpreted.  Allowable initial characters are:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">NUMBER</code></dt>
<dd><p>A line beginning with a number denotes a transaction.  It may be
followed by any number of lines, each beginning with white-space, to
denote the transaction&rsquo;s account postings.  The format of the first
line is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">DATE[=EDATE] [*|!] [(CODE)] DESC
</pre></div>

<p>If &lsquo;<samp class="samp">*</samp>&rsquo; appears after the date (with optional effective date), it
indicates the transaction is &ldquo;cleared&rdquo;, which can mean whatever the
user wants it to mean.  If &lsquo;<samp class="samp">!</samp>&rsquo; appears after the date, it
indicates the transaction is &ldquo;pending&rdquo;; i.e., tentatively cleared
from the user&rsquo;s point of view, but not yet actually cleared.  If
a <code class="code">CODE</code> appears in parentheses, it may be used to indicate
a check number, or the type of the posting.  Following these is the
payee, or a description of the posting.
</p>
<p>The format of each following posting is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">  ACCOUNT  AMOUNT  [; NOTE]
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">ACCOUNT</code> may be surrounded by parentheses if it is a virtual
posting, or square brackets if it is a virtual posting that
must balance.  The <code class="code">AMOUNT</code> can be followed by a per-unit
posting cost, by specifying <code class="code">@ AMOUNT</code>, or a complete
posting cost with <code class="code">@@ AMOUNT</code>.  Lastly, the <code class="code">NOTE</code> may
specify an actual and/or effective date for the posting by using
the syntax <code class="code">[ACTUAL_DATE]</code> or <code class="code">[=EFFECTIVE_DATE]</code> or
<code class="code">[ACTUAL_DATE=EFFECTIVE_DATE]</code> (see <a class="pxref" href="#Virtual-postings">Virtual postings</a>).
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002ddownload'><span><code class="code">P</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002ddownload'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-P"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-historical-prices"></a>
<p>Specifies a historical price for a commodity.  These are usually found
in a pricing history file (see the <samp class="option">--download (-Q)</samp> option).
The syntax is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">P DATE SYMBOL PRICE
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-_003d'><span><code class="code">=</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_003d'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-automated-transaction"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-transaction_002c-automated"></a>
<p>An automated transaction.  A value expression must appear after the
equal sign.
</p>
<p>After this initial line there should be a set of one or more postings,
just as if it were a normal transaction.  If the amounts of the postings
have no commodity, they will be applied as multipliers to whichever real
posting is matched by the value expression (see <a class="pxref" href="#Automated-Transactions">Automated Transactions</a>).
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_007e'><span><code class="code">~</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_007e'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-periodic-transaction"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-transaction_002c-periodic"></a>
<p>A periodic transaction.  A period expression must appear after the tilde.
</p>
<p>After this initial line there should be a set of one or more
postings, just as if it were a normal transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-comment'><span><code class="code">; # % | *</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-comment'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-comments"></a>
<p>A line beginning with a semicolon, pound, percent, bar or asterisk
indicates a comment, and is ignored.  Comments will not be returned in
a &ldquo;print&rdquo; response.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-tags'><span><code class="code">indented ;</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-tags'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>If the semicolon is indented and occurs inside a transaction, it is
parsed as a persistent note for its preceding category.  These notes or
tags can be used to augment the reporting and filtering capabilities of
Ledger.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Command-Directives">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Transactions-and-Comments" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Transactions and Comments</a>, Up: <a href="#Journal-Format" accesskey="u" rel="up">Journal Format</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Command-Directives-1">4.7.2 Command Directives</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dstrict-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dpedantic"></a>

<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">beginning of line</code></dt>
<dd><p>Command directives must occur at the beginning of a line.  Use of
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">!</samp>&rsquo; and &lsquo;<samp class="samp">@</samp>&rsquo; is deprecated.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-account'><span><code class="code">account</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-account'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-pre_002ddeclare-account"></a>
<p>Pre-declare valid account names.  This only has an effect if
<samp class="option">--strict</samp> or <samp class="option">--pedantic</samp> is used (see below).  The
<code class="code">account</code> directive supports several optional sub-directives, if
they immediately follow the account directive and if they begin with
whitespace:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">account Expenses:Food
    note This account is all about the chicken!
    alias food
    payee ^(KFC|Popeyes)$
    check commodity == &quot;$&quot;
    assert commodity == &quot;$&quot;
    eval print(&quot;Hello!&quot;)
    default
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">note</code> sub-directive associates a textual note with the
account.  This can be accessed later using the <code class="code">note</code> value
expression function in any account context.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">alias</code> sub-directive, which can occur multiple times, allows
the alias to be used in place of the full account name anywhere that
account names are allowed.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">payee</code> sub-directive, which can occur multiple times,
provides regexes that identify the account if that payee is
encountered and an account within its transaction ends in the name
&quot;Unknown&quot;.  Example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2012-02-27 KFC
    Expenses:Unknown      $10.00  ; Read now as &quot;Expenses:Food&quot;
    Assets:Cash
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">check</code> and <code class="code">assert</code> directives warn or raise an error
(respectively) if the given value expression evaluates to false within
the context of any posting.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">eval</code> directive evaluates the value expression in the
context of the account at the time of definition.  At the moment this
has little value.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">default</code> directive specifies that this account should be
used as the &ldquo;balancing account&rdquo; for any future transactions that
contain only a single posting.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-apply-account'><span><code class="code">apply account</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-apply-account'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Sets the root for all accounts following this directive.  Ledger
supports a hierarchical tree of accounts.  It may be convenient to
keep two &ldquo;root accounts&rdquo;.  For example you may be tracking your
personal finances and your business finances.  In order to keep them
separate you could preface all personal accounts with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">personal:</samp>&rsquo;
and all business accounts with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">business:</samp>&rsquo;.  You can easily split
out large groups of transactions without manually editing them using
the account directive.  For example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">apply account Personal
2011/11/15  Supermarket
    Expenses:Groceries      $ 50.00
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>Would result in all postings going into
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">Personal:Expenses:Groceries</samp>&rsquo; and &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Personal:Assets:Checking</samp>&rsquo;
until an &lsquo;<samp class="samp">end apply account</samp>&rsquo; directive was found.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-fixed'><span><code class="code">apply fixed</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-fixed'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-fixated-prices"></a>

<p>A fixed block is used to set fixated prices (see <a class="pxref" href="#Fixated-prices-and-costs">Fixated prices and costs</a>) for a series of transactions.  It&rsquo;s purely a typing saver, for
use when entering many transactions with fixated prices.
</p>
<p>Thus, the following:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">apply fixed CAD $0.90
2012-04-10 Lunch in Canada
    Assets:Wallet            -15.50 CAD
    Expenses:Food            15.50 CAD

2012-04-11 Second day Dinner in Canada
    Assets:Wallet            -25.75 CAD
    Expenses:Food            25.75 CAD
end apply fixed
</pre></div>

<p>is equivalent to this:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2012-04-10 Lunch in Canada
    Assets:Wallet            -15.50 CAD {=$0.90}
    Expenses:Food            15.50 CAD  {=$0.90}

2012-04-11 Second day Dinner in Canada
    Assets:Wallet            -25.75 CAD  {=$0.90}
    Expenses:Food            25.75 CAD   {=$0.90}
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-alias'><span><code class="code">alias</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-alias'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-account_002c-alias"></a>
<p>Define an alias for an account name.  If you have a deeply nested tree
of accounts, it may be convenient to define an alias, for example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">alias Dining=Expenses:Entertainment:Dining
alias Checking=Assets:Credit Union:Joint Checking Account

2011/11/28 YummyPalace
    Dining        $10.00
    Checking
</pre></div>

<p>The aliases are only in effect for transactions read in after the alias
is defined and are affected by <code class="code">account</code> directives that precede
them.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger bal --no-total ^Exp
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">              $10.00  Expenses:Entertainment:Dining
</pre></div>

<p>With the option <samp class="option">--recursive-aliases</samp>, aliases can refer to other
aliases, the following example produces exactly the same transactions
and account names as the preceding one:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">alias Entertainment=Expenses:Entertainment
alias Dining=Entertainment:Dining
alias Checking=Assets:Credit Union:Joint Checking Account

2011/11/30 ChopChop
  Dining          $10.00
  Checking
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger balance --no-total --recursive-aliases ^Exp
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">              $10.00  Expenses:Entertainment:Dining
</pre></div>

<p>The option <samp class="option">--no-aliases</samp> completely disables alias expansion.
All accounts are read verbatim as they are in the ledger file.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-assert'><span><code class="code">assert</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-assert'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-assertions"></a>
<p>An assertion can throw an error if a condition is not met during
Ledger&rsquo;s run.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">assert &lt;VALUE EXPRESSION BOOLEAN RESULT&gt;
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">bucket</code></dt>
<dd><a class="anchor" id="bucket"></a><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-bucket-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-bucket"></a>
<p>Defines the default account to use for balancing transactions.
Normally, each transaction has at least two postings, which must
balance to zero.  Ledger allows you to leave one posting with no
amount and automatically balance the transaction in the
posting.  The <code class="code">bucket</code> allows you to fill in all postings and
automatically generate an additional posting to the bucket account
balancing the transaction.  If any transaction is unbalanced, it
will automatically be balanced against the <code class="code">bucket</code> account.
The following example sets &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Assets:Checking</samp>&rsquo; as the bucket:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">bucket Assets:Checking
2011/01/25 Tom's Used Cars
    Expenses:Auto                    $ 5,500.00

2011/01/27 Book Store
    Expenses:Books                       $20.00

2011/12/01 Sale
    Assets:Checking:Business            $ 30.00
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">capture</code></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-capture"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-print"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-register-1"></a>

<p>Directs Ledger to replace any account matching a regex with the given
account.  For example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">capture  Expenses:Deductible:Medical  Medical
</pre></div>

<p>Would cause any posting with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Medical</samp>&rsquo; in its name to be replaced
with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Expenses:Deductible:Medical</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>Ledger will display the mapped payees in <code class="command">print</code> and
<code class="command">register</code> reports.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-check'><span><code class="code">check</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-check'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-assertions-1"></a>
<p>A check issues a warning if a condition is not met during Ledger&rsquo;s
run.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">check &lt;VALUE EXPRESSION BOOLEAN RESULT&gt;
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-comment-1'><span><code class="code">comment</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-comment-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-comments-1"></a>
<p>Start a block comment, closed by <code class="code">end comment</code>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-commodity-1'><span><code class="code">commodity</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-commodity-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-pre_002ddeclare-commodity"></a>
<p>Pre-declare commodity names.  This only has an effect if
<samp class="option">--strict</samp> or <samp class="option">--pedantic</samp> is used (see below).
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">commodity $
commodity CAD
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">commodity</code> directive supports several optional
sub-directives, if they immediately follow the commodity directive
and&mdash;if they are on successive lines&mdash;begin with whitespace:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">commodity $
   note American Dollars
   format $1,000.00
   nomarket
   alias USD
   default
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">note</code> sub-directive associates a textual note with the
commodity.  At present this has no value other than documentation.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">format</code> sub-directive gives you a way to tell Ledger how to
format this commodity.  In the future, using this directive will disable
Ledger&rsquo;s observation of other ways that commodity is used, and will
provide the &ldquo;canonical&rdquo; representation.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">nomarket</code> sub-directive states that the commodity&rsquo;s price
should never be auto-downloaded.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">alias</code> sub-directive states that any commodity matching this
symbol is to use the commodity declared in this block.
</p>
<p>The <code class="code">default</code> sub-directive marks this as the &ldquo;default&rdquo; commodity.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-define'><span><code class="code">define</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-define'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Allows you to define value expressions for future use.  For example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">define var_name=$100

2011/12/01 Test
    Expenses  (var_name*4)
    Assets
</pre></div>

<p>The posting will have a cost of $400.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-end'><span><code class="code">end</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-end'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Closes block commands like <code class="code">apply</code> or <code class="code">comment</code>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-expr'><span><code class="code">expr</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-expr'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Same as <code class="code">eval</code>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-include'><span><code class="code">include</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-include'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Include the stated file as if it were part of the current file.  The file
name can contain a wildcard (&lsquo;<samp class="samp">*</samp>&rsquo;) to refer to multiple files (e.g.
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">bank/*.ledger</samp>&rsquo;).
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-payee'><span><code class="code">payee</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-payee'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-print-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-register-2"></a>

<p>The <code class="code">payee</code> directive supports two optional sub-directives, if they
immediately follow the payee directive and&mdash;if it is on a successive
line&mdash;begins with whitespace:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">payee KFC
    alias KENTUCKY FRIED CHICKEN
    uuid 2a2e21d434356f886c84371eebac6e44f1337fda
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">alias</code> sub-directive provides a regex which, if it matches
a parsed payee, the declared payee name is substituted:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2012-02-27 KENTUCKY FRIED CHICKEN  ; will be read as being 'KFC'
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">uuid</code> sub-directive specifies that a transaction with exactly
the uuid given should have the declared payee name substituted:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014-05-13 UNHELPFUL PAYEE  ; will be read as being 'KFC'
    ; UUID: 2a2e21d434356f886c84371eebac6e44f1337fda
</pre></div>

<p>Ledger will display the mapped payees in <code class="command">print</code> and
<code class="command">register</code> reports.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-apply-tag'><span><code class="code">apply tag</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-apply-tag'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Allows you to designate a block of transactions and assign the same
tag to all.  Tags can have values and may be nested.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">apply tag hastag
apply tag nestedtag: true

2011/01/25 Tom's Used Cars
    Expenses:Auto                    $ 5,500.00
    ; :nobudget:
    Assets:Checking

2011/01/27 Book Store
    Expenses:Books                       $20.00
    Liabilities:MasterCard

end apply tag

2011/12/01 Sale
    Assets:Checking:Business            $ 30.00
    Income:Sales

end apply tag
</pre></div>

<p>is the equivalent of:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2011/01/25 Tom's Used Cars
    ; :hastag:
    ; nestedtag: true
    Expenses:Auto                    $ 5,500.00
    ; :nobudget:
    Assets:Checking

2011/01/27 Book Store
    ; :hastag:
    ; nestedtag: true
    Expenses:Books                       $20.00
    Liabilities:MasterCard

2011/12/01 Sale
    ; :hastag:
    Assets:Checking:Business            $ 30.00
    Income:Sales
</pre></div>



</dd>
<dt id='index-tag'><span><code class="code">tag</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-tag'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-pre_002ddeclare-tag"></a>
<p>Pre-declares tag names.  This only has an effect if <samp class="option">--strict</samp> or
<samp class="option">--pedantic</samp> is used (see below).
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">tag Receipt
tag CSV
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">tag</code> directive supports two optional sub-directives, if they
immediately follow the tag directive and&mdash;if on a successive
line&mdash;begin with whitespace:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">tag Receipt
  check value =~ /pattern/
  assert value != &quot;foobar&quot;
</pre></div>

<p>The <code class="code">check</code> and <code class="code">assert</code> sub-directives warn or error
(respectively) if the given value expression evaluates to false within
the context of any use of the related tag.  In such a context,
&ldquo;value&rdquo; is bound to the value of the tag (which may be something else
but a string if typed metadata is used!).  Such checks or assertions are
not called if no value is given.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-test'><span><code class="code">test</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-test'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-comments-2"></a>
<p>This is a synonym for <code class="code">comment</code> and must be closed by an
<code class="code">end</code> tag.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-year'><span><code class="code">year</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-year'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="anchor" id="year"></a><p>Denotes the year used for all subsequent transactions that give a date
without a year.  The year should appear immediately after the
directive, for example: <code class="code">year 2004</code>.  This is useful at the
beginning of a file, to specify the year for that file.  If all
transactions specify a year, however, this command has no effect.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>The following single letter commands may be at the beginning of a line
alone, for backwards compatibility with older Ledger versions.
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt id='index-A'><span><code class="code">A</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-A'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-bucket-2"></a>
<p>See <a class="xref" href="#bucket">bucket</a>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-Y'><span><code class="code">Y</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-Y'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-year-1"></a>
<p>See <a class="xref" href="#year">year</a>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-N'><span><code class="code">N SYMBOL</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-N'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Indicates that pricing information is to be ignored for a given
symbol, nor will quotes ever be downloaded for that symbol.  Useful
with a home currency, such as the dollar &lsquo;<samp class="samp">$</samp>&rsquo;.  It is recommended
that these pricing options be set in the price database file, which
defaults to <samp class="file">~/.pricedb</samp>.  The syntax for this command is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">N SYMBOL
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-xact'><span><code class="code">D AMOUNT</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-xact'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-D"></a>
<p>Specifies the default commodity to use, by specifying an amount in the
expected format.  The <code class="command">xact</code> command will use this commodity as
the default when none other can be determined.  This command may be used
multiple times, to set the default flags for different commodities;
whichever is seen last is used as the default commodity.  For example,
to set US dollars as the default commodity, while also setting the
thousands flag and decimal flag for that commodity, use:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">D $1,000.00
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-C-1'><span><code class="code">C AMOUNT1 = AMOUNT2</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-C-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Specifies a commodity conversion, where the first amount is given to
be equivalent to the second amount.  The first amount should use the
decimal precision desired during reporting:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">C 1.00 Kb = 1024 bytes
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-I'><span><code class="code">I, i, O, o, b, h</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-I'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-i"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-O"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-o"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-b"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-h"></a>
<p>These four relate to timeclock support, which permits Ledger to read
timelog files.  See timeclock&rsquo;s documentation for more info on the
syntax of its timelog files.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Converting-from-other-formats">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Archiving-Previous-Years" accesskey="n" rel="next">Archiving Previous Years</a>, Previous: <a href="#Journal-Format" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Journal Format</a>, Up: <a href="#Keeping-a-Journal" accesskey="u" rel="up">Keeping a Journal</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Converting-from-other-formats-1">4.8 Converting from other formats</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-csv-importing"></a>

<p>There are numerous tools to help convert various formats to a Ledger
file.  Most banks will generate a comma separated values file that can
easily be parsed into Ledger format using one of those tools.  Some of
the most popular tools are:
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li><code class="code">ledger convert download.csv</code>
</li><li><code class="code">hledger -f checking.csv print</code>
</li><li><a class="uref" href="https://github.com/quentinsf/icsv2ledger"><code class="code">icsv2ledger</code></a>
</li><li><a class="uref" href="https://github.com/tazzben/csvToLedger"><code class="code">csvToLedger</code></a>
</li><li><a class="uref" href="https://launchpad.net/csv2ledger"><code class="code">CSV2Ledger</code></a>
</li></ul>

<p>Directly pulling information from banks is outside the scope of
Ledger&rsquo;s function.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Archiving-Previous-Years">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Converting-from-other-formats" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Converting from other formats</a>, Up: <a href="#Keeping-a-Journal" accesskey="u" rel="up">Keeping a Journal</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Archiving-Previous-Years-1">4.9 Archiving Previous Years</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-equity"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-print-2"></a>

<p>After a while, your journal can get to be pretty large.  While this
will not slow down Ledger&mdash;it&rsquo;s designed to process journals very
quickly&mdash;things can start to feel &ldquo;messy&rdquo;; and it&rsquo;s a universal
complaint that when finances feel messy, people avoid them.
</p>
<p>Thus, archiving the data from previous years into their own files can
offer a sense of completion, and freedom from the past.  But how to
best accomplish this with the ledger program?  There are two commands
that make it very simple: <code class="command">print</code>, and <code class="command">equity</code>.
</p>
<p>Let&rsquo;s take an example file, with data ranging from year 2000 until
2004.  We want to archive years 2000 and 2001 to their own file,
leaving 2002&ndash;2004 in the current file.  So, use <code class="command">print</code> to
output all the earlier transactions to a file called
<samp class="file">ledger-old.dat</samp>:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f ledger.dat -b 2000 -e 2002 print &gt; ledger-old.dat
</pre></div>

<p>Note that <samp class="option">-e</samp> limits output to transactions <em class="emph">before</em> the
date specified.
</p>
<p>To delete older data from the current ledger file, use <code class="command">print</code>
again, this time specifying year 2002 as the starting date:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f ledger.dat -b 2002 print &gt; x
$ mv x ledger.dat
</pre></div>

<p>However, now the current file contains <em class="emph">only</em> postings from 2002
onward, which will not yield accurate present-day balances, because the
net income from previous years is no longer being tallied.  To
compensate for this, we must append an equity report for the old ledger
at the beginning of the new one:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f ledger-old.dat equity &gt; equity.dat
$ cat equity.dat ledger.dat &gt; x
$ mv x ledger.dat
$ rm equity.dat
</pre></div>

<p>Now the balances reported from <samp class="file">ledger.dat</samp> are identical to what
they were before the data was split.
</p>
<p>How often should you split your ledger?  You never need to, if you
don&rsquo;t want to.  Even eighty years of data will not slow down ledger
much, and that&rsquo;s just using present day hardware!  Or, you can keep
the previous and current year in one file, and each year before that
in its own file.  It&rsquo;s really up to you, and how you want to organize
your finances.  For those who also keep an accurate paper trail, it
might be useful to archive the older years to their own files, then
burn those files to a CD to keep with the paper records&mdash;along with
any electronic statements received during the year.  In the arena of
organization, just keep in mind this maxim: Do whatever keeps you
doing it.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="chapter-level-extent" id="Transactions">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

</div>
<h2 class="chapter" id="Transactions-1">5 Transactions</h2>


<ul class="mini-toc">
