</div>
<h2 class="chapter" id="Reporting-Commands-1">7 Reporting Commands</h2>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="1">Primary Financial Reports</a></li>
<li><a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="2">Reports in other Formats</a></li>
<li><a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="3">Reports about your Journals</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Primary-Financial-Reports">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="n" rel="next">Reports in other Formats</a>, Previous: <a href="#Reporting-Commands" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Reporting Commands</a>, Up: <a href="#Reporting-Commands" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reporting Commands</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Primary-Financial-Reports-1">7.1 Primary Financial Reports</h3>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#The-balance-command" accesskey="1">The <code class="command">balance</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-equity-command" accesskey="2">The <code class="command">equity</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-register-command" accesskey="3">The <code class="command">register</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-print-command" accesskey="4">The <code class="command">print</code> command</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-balance-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-equity-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">equity</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Primary Financial Reports</a>, Up: <a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="u" rel="up">Primary Financial Reports</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-balance-command-1">7.1.1 The <code class="command">balance</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-balance-1"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">balance</code> command reports the current balance of all
accounts.  It accepts a list of optional regexes, which confine the
balance report to the matching accounts.  If an account contains
multiple types of commodities, each commodity&rsquo;s total is reported
separately.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-equity-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-register-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">register</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#The-balance-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">balance</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="u" rel="up">Primary Financial Reports</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-equity-command-1">7.1.2 The <code class="command">equity</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-equity-1"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">equity</code> command prints out account balances as if they
were transactions.  This makes it easy to establish the starting
balances for an account, such as when <a class="ref" href="#Archiving-Previous-Years">Archiving Previous Years</a>.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-register-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-print-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">print</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#The-equity-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">equity</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="u" rel="up">Primary Financial Reports</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-register-command-1">7.1.3 The <code class="command">register</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-register-4"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002damount_002ddata-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dtotal_002ddata-1"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">register</code> command displays all the postings occurring in
a single account, line by line.  The account regex must be specified as
the only argument to this command.  If any regexes occur after the
required account name, the register will contain only those postings
that match, which makes it very useful for hunting down a particular
posting.
</p>
<p>The output from <code class="command">register</code> is very close to what a typical
checkbook, or single-account ledger, would look like.  It also shows a
running balance.  The final running balance of any register should
always be the same as the current balance of that account.
</p>
<p>If you have &ldquo;Gnuplot&rdquo; installed, you may plot the amount or running
total of any register by using the script <samp class="file">report</samp>, which is
included in the Ledger distribution.  The only requirement is that you
add either <samp class="option">--amount-data (-j)</samp> or <samp class="option">--total-data (-J)</samp> to
your <code class="command">register</code> command, in order to plot either the amount or
total column, respectively.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-print-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#The-register-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">register</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="u" rel="up">Primary Financial Reports</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-print-command-1">7.1.4 The <code class="command">print</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-print-3"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">print</code> command prints out ledger transactions in a textual
format that can be parsed by Ledger.  They will be properly formatted,
and output in the most economic form possible.  The <code class="command">print</code>
command also takes a list of optional regexes, which will cause only
those postings which match in some way to be printed.
</p>
<p>The <code class="command">print</code> command can be a handy way to clean up a ledger
file whose formatting has gotten out of hand.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Reports-in-other-Formats">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="n" rel="next">Reports about your Journals</a>, Previous: <a href="#Primary-Financial-Reports" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Primary Financial Reports</a>, Up: <a href="#Reporting-Commands" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reporting Commands</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Reports-in-other-Formats-1">7.2 Reports in other Formats</h3>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Comma-Separated-Values-files" accesskey="1">Comma Separated Values files</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-lisp-command" accesskey="2">The <code class="command">lisp</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#Emacs-org-Mode" accesskey="3">Emacs <code class="command">org</code> Mode</a></li>
<li><a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="4">Org mode with Babel</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-pricemap-command" accesskey="5">The <code class="command">pricemap</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-xml-command" accesskey="6">The <code class="command">xml</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#prices-and-pricedb-commands" accesskey="7"><code class="command">prices</code> and <code class="command">pricedb</code> commands</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Comma-Separated-Values-files">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-lisp-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">lisp</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Reports in other Formats</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Comma-Separated-Values-files-1">7.2.1 Comma Separated Values files</h4>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#The-csv-command" accesskey="1">The <code class="command">csv</code> command</a></li>
<li><a href="#The-convert-command" accesskey="2">The <code class="command">convert</code> command</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="The-csv-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-convert-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">convert</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#Comma-Separated-Values-files" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Comma Separated Values files</a>, Up: <a href="#Comma-Separated-Values-files" accesskey="u" rel="up">Comma Separated Values files</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="The-csv-command-1">7.2.1.1 The <code class="command">csv</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-csv"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">csv</code> command prints the desired ledger
transactions in a csv format suitable for importing into other programs.
You can specify the transactions to print using all the normal
limiting and searching functions.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="The-convert-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#The-csv-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">csv</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Comma-Separated-Values-files" accesskey="u" rel="up">Comma Separated Values files</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="The-convert-command-1">7.2.1.2 The <code class="command">convert</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-csv-importing-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-comma-separated-variable-file-reading"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-convert"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dinput_002ddate_002dformat-DATE_005fFORMAT"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">convert</code> command parses a comma separated value (csv) file
and prints Ledger transactions.  Many banks offer csv file downloads.
Unfortunately, the file formats, aside from the commas, are all
different.  The ledger <code class="command">convert</code> command tries to help as much
as it can.
</p>
<p>Your bank&rsquo;s csv files will have fields in different orders from other
banks, so there must be a way to tell Ledger what to expect.  Insert
a line at the beginning of the csv file that describes the fields to
Ledger.
</p>
<p>For example, this is a portion of a csv file downloaded from a credit
union in the United States:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Account Name: VALUFIRST CHECKING
Account Number: 71
Date Range: 11/13/2011 - 12/13/2011

Transaction Number,Date,Description,Memo,Amount Debit,Amount Credit,Balance,Check Number,Fees
767406,12/13/2011,&quot;Deposit&quot;,&quot;CASH DEPOSIT&quot;,,45.00,00001646.89,,
767718,12/13/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;ACE HARDWARE 16335 S HOUGHTON RD&quot;,8.80,,00001640.04,,
767406,12/13/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;ACE HARDWARE 16335 S HOUGHTON RD&quot;,1.03,,00001648.84,,
683342,12/13/2011,&quot;Visa Checking&quot;,&quot;NetFlix Date 12/12/11 000326585896 5968&quot;,21.85,,00001649.87,,
639668,12/13/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;ID: 1741472662 CO: XXAA.COM PAYMNT&quot;,236.65,,00001671.72,,
1113648,12/12/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;Tuscan IT #00037657&quot;,29.73,,00001908.37,,
</pre></div>

<p>Unfortunately, as it stands Ledger cannot read it, but you can.  Ledger
expects the first line to contain a description of the fields on each
line of the file.  The fields ledger can recognize contain these
case-insensitive strings <code class="code">date</code>, <code class="code">posted</code>, <code class="code">code</code>,
<code class="code">payee</code> or <code class="code">desc</code> or <code class="code">description</code>, <code class="code">amount</code> or
<code class="code">credit</code>, <code class="code">debit</code>, <code class="code">cost</code>, <code class="code">total</code>, and <code class="code">note</code>.
</p>
<p>Delete the account description lines at the top, and replace the first
line in the data above with:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">,date,payee,note,debit,credit,,code,
</pre></div>

<p>Then execute ledger like this:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger convert download.csv --input-date-format &quot;%m/%d/%Y&quot;
</pre></div>

<p>Where the <samp class="option">--input-date-format <var class="var">DATE_FORMAT</var></samp> option tells
ledger how to interpret the dates.
</p>
<p>Importing csv files is a lot of work, but is very amenable to
scripting.
</p>
<p>If your csv has only one amount column with opposite signs for credits
and debits, this is also supported. For example, the first fiew lines
of the above account could also be in the following format:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">,date,payee,note,credit,,code,
767406,12/13/2011,&quot;Deposit&quot;,&quot;CASH DEPOSIT&quot;,45.00,00001646.89,,
767718,12/13/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;ACE HARDWARE 16335 S HOUGHTON RD&quot;,-8.80,00001640.04,,
</pre></div>

<p>If there are columns in the bank data you would like to keep in your
ledger data, besides the primary fields described above, you can name
them in the field descriptor list and Ledger will include them in the
transaction as meta data if it doesn&rsquo;t recognize the field name.  For
example, if you want to capture the bank transaction number and it
occurs in the first column of the data use:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">transid,date,payee,note,debit,credit,,code,
</pre></div>

<p>Ledger will include &lsquo;<samp class="samp">; transid: 767718</samp>&rsquo; in the first transaction
from the file above.
</p>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dinvert"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dauto_002dmatch"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002daccount-STR"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002drich_002ddata"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">convert</code> command accepts four options.  They are
<samp class="option">--invert</samp> which inverts the amount, <samp class="option">--auto-match</samp>
which automatically matches an account from the Ledger journal for every
CSV line, <samp class="option">--account <var class="var">STR</var></samp> which you can use to specify the
account to balance against, and <samp class="option">--rich-data</samp> which stores
additional tag/value pairs.
</p>
<p>Using the two first lines of the above csv file,
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">,date,payee,note,debit,credit,balance,code,
767406,12/13/2011,&quot;Deposit&quot;,&quot;CASH DEPOSIT&quot;,,45.00,00001646.89,,
767718,12/13/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;ACE HARDWARE 16335 S HOUGHTON RD&quot;,8.80,,00001640.04,,
</pre></div>

<p>and launching the below command,
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger convert download.csv --input-date-format &quot;%m/%d/%Y&quot; \
  --invert --account Assets:MyBank --rich-data \
  --file sample.dat --now=2012/01/13
</pre></div>

<p>you will get the result:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2011/12/13 * Deposit  ;CASH DEPOSIT
    ; balance: 00001646.89
    ; CSV: 767406,12/13/2011,&quot;Deposit&quot;,&quot;CASH DEPOSIT&quot;,,45.00,00001646.89,,
    ; Imported: 2012/01/13
    ; UUID: ce0b7d42b02ce5eaf0d828c3b1028041fd09494c
    Expenses:Unknown                             -45
    Assets:MyBank

2011/12/13 * Withdrawal  ;ACE HARDWARE 16335 S HOUGHTON RD
    ; balance: 00001640.04
    ; CSV: 767718,12/13/2011,&quot;Withdrawal&quot;,&quot;ACE HARDWARE 16335 S HOUGHTON RD&quot;,8.80,,00001640.04,,
    ; Imported: 2012/01/13
    ; UUID: 0aaf85911adc447ea2d5377ff6a60d6b2940047f
    Expenses:Unknown                             8.8
    Assets:MyBank
</pre></div>

<p>The three added metadata are: &lsquo;<samp class="samp">CSV</samp>&rsquo; as the original line from csv
file, &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Imported</samp>&rsquo; as the date when the csv file was imported into
Ledger, and &lsquo;<samp class="samp">UUID</samp>&rsquo; as a checksum of original csv line.
</p>
<p>If an entry with the same &lsquo;<samp class="samp">UUID</samp>&rsquo; tag is already included in the
normal ledger file (specified via <samp class="option">--file <var class="var">FILE</var> (-f)</samp> or via
the environment variable <code class="env">LEDGER_FILE</code>) this entry will not be
printed again.
</p>
<p>In the output above, the account is &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Expenses:Unknown</samp>&rsquo; for CSV
lines.  You can use the <samp class="option">--auto-match</samp> option to automatically
match an account from your Ledger journal.
</p>
<p>You can also use <code class="command">convert</code> with <code class="code">payee</code> and <code class="code">account</code>
directives.  First, you can use the <code class="code">payee</code> and <code class="code">alias</code>
directive to rewrite the <code class="code">payee</code> field based on some rules.  Then
you can use the account and its <code class="code">payee</code> directive to specify the
account.  I use it like this, for example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">payee Aldi
    alias ^ALDI SUED SAGT DANKE
account Aufwand:Einkauf:Lebensmittel
    payee ^(Aldi|Alnatura|Kaufland|REWE)$
</pre></div>

<p>Note that it may be necessary for the output of &lsquo;<samp class="samp">ledger convert</samp>&rsquo;
to be passed through <code class="code">ledger print</code> a second time if you want to
match on the new payee field.  During the <code class="code">ledger convert</code> run,
only the original payee name as specified in the csv data seems to be
used.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-lisp-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Emacs-org-Mode" accesskey="n" rel="next">Emacs <code class="command">org</code> Mode</a>, Previous: <a href="#Comma-Separated-Values-files" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Comma Separated Values files</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-lisp-command-1">7.2.2 The <code class="command">lisp</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-lisp"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-emacs"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">lisp</code> command prints results in a form that can be read
directly by Emacs Lisp.  The format of the <code class="code">sexp</code> is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">((BEG-POS CLEARED DATE CODE PAYEE
  (ACCOUNT AMOUNT)...)  ; list of postings
 ...)                   ; list of transactions
</pre></div>

<p><code class="command">emacs</code> can also be used as a synonym for <code class="command">lisp</code>.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Emacs-org-Mode">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="n" rel="next">Org mode with Babel</a>, Previous: <a href="#The-lisp-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">lisp</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Emacs-org-Mode-1">7.2.3 Emacs <code class="command">org</code> Mode</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-org"></a>

<p>Org mode has a sub-system known as Babel which allows for literate
programming.  This allows you to mix text and code within the same
document and automatically execute code which may generate results
which will then appear in the text.
</p>
<p>One of the languages supported by Babel is Ledger, so that you can have
ledger commands embedded in a text file and have the output of ledger
commands also appear in the text file.  The output can be updated
whenever any new ledger entries are added.
</p>
<p>For instance, the following Org mode text document snippet illustrates
a very naive but still useful application of the Babel system:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">* A simple test of ledger in an org file
The following are some entries and I have requested that ledger be run
to generate a balance on the accounts.  I could have asked for
a register or, in fact, anything at all the ledger can do through
command-line options.

#+begin_src ledger :cmdline bal :results value
2010/01/01 * Starting balance
  assets:bank:savings       Â£1300.00
  income:starting balances
2010/07/22 * Got paid
  assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00
  income:salary
2010/07/23 Rent
  expenses:rent              Â£500.00
  assets:bank:chequing
#+end_src

#+results:
:            Â£1800.00  assets:bank
:             Â£500.00    chequing
:            Â£1300.00    savings
:             Â£500.00  expenses:rent
:           Â£-2300.00  income
:           Â£-1000.00    salary
:           Â£-1300.00    starting balances
</pre></div>

<p>Typing <kbd class="kbd">C-c C-c</kbd> anywhere in the &ldquo;ledger source code block&rdquo; will
invoke ledger on the contents of that block and generate a &ldquo;results&rdquo;
block.  The results block can appear anywhere in the file but, by
default, will appear immediately below the source code block.
</p>
<p>You can combine multiple source code blocks before executing ledger and
do all kinds of other wonderful things with Babel (and Org mode).
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Org-mode-with-Babel">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-pricemap-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">pricemap</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#Emacs-org-Mode" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Emacs <code class="command">org</code> Mode</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Org-mode-with-Babel-1">7.2.4 Org mode with Babel</h4>

<p>Using Babel, it is possible to record financial transactions
conveniently in an org file and subsequently generate the financial
reports required.
</p>
<p>As of Org mode 7.01, Ledger support is provided.  Check the
<a class="uref" href="https://orgmode.org/worg/org-contrib/babel/">Babel documentation
on Worg</a> for instructions on how to achieve this but I currently do
this directly as follows:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">(org-babel-do-load-languages
 'org-babel-load-languages
 '((ledger . t)         ;this is the important one for this tutorial
  ))
</pre></div>

<p>Once Ledger support in Babel has been enabled, we can proceed to
include Ledger entries within an org file.  There are three ways (at
least) in which these can be included:
</p>
<ol class="enumerate">
<li> place all Ledger entries within one single source block and execute this
block with different arguments to generate the appropriate reports,

</li><li> place Ledger entries in more than one source block and use the
<code class="code">noweb</code> literary programming approach, supported by Babel, to
combine these into one block elsewhere in the file for processing by
Ledger,

</li><li> place Ledger entries in different source blocks and use <code class="code">tangle</code> to
generate a Ledger file which you can subsequently process using Ledger
directly.
</li></ol>

<p>The first two are described in more detail in this short tutorial.
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Embedded-Ledger-example-with-single-source-block" accesskey="1">Embedded Ledger example with single source block</a></li>
<li><a href="#Multiple-Ledger-source-blocks-with-noweb" accesskey="2">Multiple Ledger source blocks with <code class="code">noweb</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#Income-Entries" accesskey="3">Income Entries</a></li>
<li><a href="#Expenses" accesskey="4">Expenses</a></li>
<li><a href="#Financial-Summaries" accesskey="5">Financial Summaries</a></li>
<li><a href="#An-overall-balance-summary" accesskey="6">An overall balance summary</a></li>
<li><a href="#Generating-a-monthly-register" accesskey="7">Generating a monthly register</a></li>
<li><a href="#Summary" accesskey="8">Summary</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Embedded-Ledger-example-with-single-source-block">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Multiple-Ledger-source-blocks-with-noweb" accesskey="n" rel="next">Multiple Ledger source blocks with <code class="code">noweb</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Org mode with Babel</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Embedded-Ledger-example-with-single-source-block-1">7.2.4.1 Embedded Ledger example with single source block</h4>

<p>The easiest, albeit possibly least useful, way in which to use Ledger
within an org file is to use a single source block to record all Ledger
entries.  The following is an example source block:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+name: allinone
#+begin_src ledger
2010/01/01 * Starting balance
  assets:bank:savings       Â£1300.00
  income:starting balances
2010/07/22 * Got paid
  assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00
  income:salary
2010/07/23 Rent
  expenses:rent              Â£500.00
  assets:bank:chequing
2010/07/24 Food
  expenses:food              Â£150.00
  assets:bank:chequing
2010/07/31 * Interest on bank savings
  assets:bank:savings          Â£3.53
  income:interest
2010/07/31 * Transfer savings
  assets:bank:savings        Â£250.00
  assets:bank:chequing
2010/08/01 got paid again
  assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00
  income:salary
#+end_src
</pre></div>

<p>In this example, we have combined both expenses and income into one set
of Ledger entries.  We can now generate register and balance reports (as
well as many other types of reports) using Babel to invoke Ledger with
specific arguments.  The arguments are passed to Ledger using the
<code class="code">:cmdline</code> header argument.  In the code block above, there is no
such argument so the system takes the default.  For Ledger code blocks,
the default <code class="code">:cmdline</code> argument is <code class="code">bal</code> and the result of
evaluating this code block (<kbd class="kbd">C-c C-c</kbd>) would be:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+results: allinone()
:            Â£2653.53  assets:bank
:            Â£1100.00    chequing
:            Â£1553.53    savings
:             Â£650.00  expenses
:             Â£150.00    food
:             Â£500.00    rent
:           Â£-3303.53  income
:              Â£-3.53    interest
:           Â£-2000.00    salary
:           Â£-1300.00    starting balances
</pre></div>

<p>If, instead, you wished to generate a register of all the transactions,
you would change the <code class="code">#+begin_src</code> line for the code block to
include the required command-line option:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+begin_src ledger :cmdline reg
</pre></div>

<p>Evaluating the code block again would generate a different report.
</p>
<p>Having to change the actual directive on the code block and re-evaluate
makes it difficult to have more than one view of your transactions and
financial state.  Eventually, Babel will support passing arguments to
<code class="code">#+call</code> evaluations of code blocks but this support is missing
currently.  Instead, we can use the concepts of literary programming, as
implemented by the <code class="code">noweb</code> features of Babel, to help us.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Multiple-Ledger-source-blocks-with-noweb">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Income-Entries" accesskey="n" rel="next">Income Entries</a>, Previous: <a href="#Embedded-Ledger-example-with-single-source-block" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Embedded Ledger example with single source block</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Multiple-Ledger-source-blocks-with-noweb-1">7.2.4.2 Multiple Ledger source blocks with <code class="code">noweb</code></h4>

<p>The <code class="code">noweb</code> feature of Babel allows us to expand references to
other code blocks within a code block.  For Ledger, this can be used to
group transactions according to type, say, and then bring various sets
of transactions together to generate reports.
</p>
<p>Using the same transactions used above, we could consider splitting
these into expenses and income, as follows:
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Income-Entries">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Expenses" accesskey="n" rel="next">Expenses</a>, Previous: <a href="#Multiple-Ledger-source-blocks-with-noweb" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Multiple Ledger source blocks with <code class="code">noweb</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Income-Entries-1">7.2.4.3 Income Entries</h4>

<p>The first set of entries relates to income, either monthly pay or
interest, all typically going into one of my bank accounts.  Here, I have
placed several entries, but we could have had each entry in a separate
<code class="code">src</code> block.  Note that all code blocks you wish to refer to later
must have the <code class="code">:noweb yes</code> header argument specified.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+name: income
#+begin_src ledger :noweb yes
2010/01/01 * Starting balance
  assets:bank:savings       Â£1300.00
  income:starting balances
2010/07/22 * Got paid
  assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00
  income:salary
2010/07/31 * Interest on bank savings
  assets:bank:savings          Â£3.53
  income:interest
2010/07/31 * Transfer savings
  assets:bank:savings        Â£250.00
  assets:bank:chequing
2010/08/01 got paid again
  assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00
  income:salary
#+end_src
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Expenses">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Financial-Summaries" accesskey="n" rel="next">Financial Summaries</a>, Previous: <a href="#Income-Entries" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Income Entries</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Expenses-1">7.2.4.4 Expenses</h4>

<p>The following entries relate to personal expenses, such as rent and
food.  Again, these have all been placed in a single <code class="code">src</code> block but
could have been done individually.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+name: expenses
#+begin_src ledger :noweb yes
2010/07/23 Rent
  expenses:rent              Â£500.00
  assets:bank:chequing
2010/07/24 Food
  expenses:food              Â£150.00
  assets:bank:chequing
#+end_src
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Financial-Summaries">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#An-overall-balance-summary" accesskey="n" rel="next">An overall balance summary</a>, Previous: <a href="#Expenses" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Expenses</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Financial-Summaries-1">7.2.4.5 Financial Summaries</h4>

<p>Given the ledger entries defined above in the income and expenses code
blocks, we can now refer to these using the noweb expansion directives,
<code class="code">&lt;&lt;name&gt;&gt;</code>.  We can now define different code blocks to generate
specific reports for those transactions.  Below are two examples, one to
generate a balance report and one to generate a register report of all
transactions.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="An-overall-balance-summary">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Generating-a-monthly-register" accesskey="n" rel="next">Generating a monthly register</a>, Previous: <a href="#Financial-Summaries" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Financial Summaries</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="An-overall-balance-summary-1">7.2.4.6 An overall balance summary</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dsubtotal-1"></a>

<p>The overall balance of your account and expenditure with a breakdown
according to category is specified by passing the <code class="code">:cmdline bal</code>
argument to Ledger.  This code block can now be evaluated (<kbd class="kbd">C-c C-c</kbd>)
and the results generated by incorporating the transactions referred to
by the <code class="code">&lt;&lt;income&gt;&gt;</code> and <code class="code">&lt;&lt;expenses&gt;&gt;</code> lines.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+name: balance
#+begin_src ledger :cmdline bal :noweb yes
&lt;&lt;income&gt;&gt;
&lt;&lt;expenses&gt;&gt;
#+end_src

#+results: balance
:            Â£2653.53  assets:bank
:            Â£1100.00    chequing
:            Â£1553.53    savings
:             Â£650.00  expenses
:             Â£150.00    food
:             Â£500.00    rent
:           Â£-3303.53  income
:              Â£-3.53    interest
:           Â£-2000.00    salary
:           Â£-1300.00    starting balances
</pre></div>

<p>If you want a less detailed breakdown of where your money is, you can
specify the <samp class="option">--collapse (-n)</samp> flag (i.e. &lsquo;<samp class="samp">:cmdline -n bal</samp>&rsquo;)
to tell Ledger to exclude sub-accounts in the report.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+begin_src ledger :cmdline -n bal :noweb yes
&lt;&lt;income&gt;&gt;
&lt;&lt;expenses&gt;&gt;
#+end_src

#+results:
:            Â£2653.53  assets
:             Â£650.00  expenses
:           Â£-3303.53  income
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Generating-a-monthly-register">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Summary" accesskey="n" rel="next">Summary</a>, Previous: <a href="#An-overall-balance-summary" accesskey="p" rel="prev">An overall balance summary</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Generating-a-monthly-register-1">7.2.4.7 Generating a monthly register</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-register-5"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dmonthly-1"></a>

<p>You can also generate a monthly register (the <code class="command">reg</code> command) by
executing the following <code class="code">src</code> block.  This presents a summary of
transactions for each monthly period (the <samp class="option">--monthly (-M)</samp>
argument) with a running total in the final column (which should be 0 at
the end if all the entries are correct).
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+name: monthlyregister
#+begin_src ledger :cmdline -M reg :noweb yes
&lt;&lt;income&gt;&gt;
&lt;&lt;expenses&gt;&gt;
#+end_src

#+results: monthlyregister
:2010/01/01 - 2010/01/31         assets:bank:savings       Â£1300.00    Â£1300.00
:                                in:starting balances     Â£-1300.00           0
:2010/07/01 - 2010/07/31         assets:bank:chequing       Â£100.00     Â£100.00
:                                assets:bank:savings        Â£253.53     Â£353.53
:                                expenses:food              Â£150.00     Â£503.53
:                                expenses:rent              Â£500.00    Â£1003.53
:                                income:interest             Â£-3.53    Â£1000.00
:                                income:salary            Â£-1000.00           0
:2010/08/01 - 2010/08/01         assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00    Â£1000.00
:                                income:salary            Â£-1000.00           0
</pre></div>

<p>We could also generate a monthly report on our assets showing how these
are increasing (or decreasing!).  In this case, the final column will be
the running total of the assets in our ledger.
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">#+name: monthlyassetsregister
#+begin_src ledger :cmdline -M reg assets :noweb yes
&lt;&lt;income&gt;&gt;
&lt;&lt;expenses&gt;&gt;
#+end_src

#+results: monthlyassetsregister
: 2010/01/01 - 2010/01/31         assets:bank:savings       Â£1300.00    Â£1300.00
: 2010/07/01 - 2010/07/31         assets:bank:chequing       Â£100.00    Â£1400.00
:                                 assets:bank:savings        Â£253.53    Â£1653.53
: 2010/08/01 - 2010/08/01         assets:bank:chequing      Â£1000.00    Â£2653.53
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Summary">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Generating-a-monthly-register" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Generating a monthly register</a>, Up: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="u" rel="up">Org mode with Babel</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Summary-1">7.2.4.8 Summary</h4>

<p>This short tutorial shows how Ledger entries can be embedded in an org
file and manipulated using Babel.  However, only simple Ledger features
have been illustrated; please refer to the Ledger documentation for
examples of more complex operations on a ledger.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-pricemap-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#The-xml-command" accesskey="n" rel="next">The <code class="command">xml</code> command</a>, Previous: <a href="#Org-mode-with-Babel" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Org mode with Babel</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-pricemap-command-1">7.2.5 The <code class="command">pricemap</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-pricemap"></a>

<p>If you have the <samp class="file">graphviz</samp> graph visualization package installed,
ledger can generate a graph of the relationship between your various
commodities.  The output file is in the &ldquo;dot&rdquo; format.
</p>
<p>This is probably not very interesting, unless you have many different
commodities valued in terms of each other.  For example, multiple
currencies and multiple investments valued in those currencies.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="The-xml-command">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#prices-and-pricedb-commands" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">prices</code> and <code class="command">pricedb</code> commands</a>, Previous: <a href="#The-pricemap-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">pricemap</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="The-xml-command-1">7.2.6 The <code class="command">xml</code> command</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-xml"></a>

<p>By default, Ledger uses a human-readable data format, and displays its
reports in a manner meant to be read on screen.  For the purpose of
writing tools which use Ledger, however, it is possible to read and
display data using XML.  This section documents that format.
</p>
<p>The general format used for Ledger data is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;?xml version=&quot;1.0&quot;?&gt;
&lt;ledger&gt;
  &lt;xact&gt;...&lt;/xact&gt;
  &lt;xact&gt;...&lt;/xact&gt;
  &lt;xact&gt;...&lt;/xact&gt;...
&lt;/ledger&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>The data stream is enclosed in a <code class="code">ledger</code> tag, which contains a
series of one or more transactions.  Each <code class="code">xact</code> describes one
transaction and contains a series of one or more postings:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;xact&gt;
  &lt;en:date&gt;2004/03/01&lt;/en:date&gt;
  &lt;en:cleared/&gt;
  &lt;en:code&gt;100&lt;/en:code&gt;
  &lt;en:payee&gt;John Wiegley&lt;/en:payee&gt;
  &lt;en:postings&gt;
    &lt;posting&gt;...&lt;/posting&gt;
    &lt;posting&gt;...&lt;/posting&gt;
    &lt;posting&gt;...&lt;/posting&gt;...
  &lt;/en:postings&gt;
&lt;/xact&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>The date format for <code class="code">en:date</code> is always <code class="code">YYYY/MM/DD</code>.  The
<code class="code">en:cleared</code> tag is optional, and indicates whether the posting has
been cleared or not.  There is also an <code class="code">en:pending</code> tag, for
marking pending postings.  The <code class="code">en:code</code> and <code class="code">en:payee</code> tags
both contain whatever text the user wishes.
</p>
<p>After the initial transaction data, there must follow a set of postings
marked with <code class="code">en:postings</code>.  Typically these postings will all
balance each other, but if not they will be automatically balanced into
an account named &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Unknown</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>Within the <code class="code">en:postings</code> tag is a series of one or more
<code class="code">posting</code>&rsquo;s, which have the following form:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;posting&gt;
  &lt;tr:account&gt;Expenses:Computer:Hardware&lt;/tr:account&gt;
  &lt;tr:amount&gt;
    &lt;value type=&quot;amount&quot;&gt;
      &lt;amount&gt;
        &lt;commodity flags=&quot;PT&quot;&gt;$&lt;/commodity&gt;
        &lt;quantity&gt;90.00&lt;/quantity&gt;
      &lt;/amount&gt;
    &lt;/value&gt;
  &lt;/tr:amount&gt;
&lt;/posting&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>This is a basic posting.  It may also begin with
<code class="code">tr:virtual</code> and/or <code class="code">tr:generated</code> tags, to indicate virtual
and auto-generated postings.  Then follows the <code class="code">tr:account</code>
tag, which contains the full name of the account the posting is
related to.  Colons separate parent from child in an account name.
</p>
<p>Lastly follows the amount of the posting, indicated by
<code class="code">tr:amount</code>.  Within this tag is a <code class="code">value</code> tag, of which
there are four different kinds, each with its own format:
</p>
<ol class="enumerate">
<li> Boolean,
</li><li> integer,
</li><li> amount,
</li><li> balance.
</li></ol>

<p>The format of a Boolean value is <code class="code">true</code> or <code class="code">false</code>
surrounded by a <code class="code">boolean</code> tag, for example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;boolean&gt;true&lt;/boolean&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>The format of an integer value is the numerical value surrounded by an
<code class="code">integer</code> tag, for example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;integer&gt;12036&lt;/integer&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>The format of an amount contains two members, the commodity and the
quantity.  The commodity can have a set of flags that indicate how to
display it.  The meaning of the flags (all of which are optional) are:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">P</code></dt>
<dd><p>The commodity is prefixed to the value.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">S</code></dt>
<dd><p>The commodity is separated from the value by a space.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">T</code></dt>
<dd><p>Thousands markers are used to display the amount.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">E</code></dt>
<dd><p>The format of the amount is European, with period used as a thousands
marker, and comma used as the decimal point.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>The actual quantity for an amount is an integer of arbitrary size.
Ledger uses the GNU multiple precision arithmetic library to handle
such values.  The XML format assumes the reader to be equally capable.
Here is an example amount:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;value type=&quot;amount&quot;&gt;
  &lt;amount&gt;
    &lt;commodity flags=&quot;PT&quot;&gt;$&lt;/commodity&gt;
    &lt;quantity&gt;90.00&lt;/quantity&gt;
  &lt;/amount&gt;
&lt;/value&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>Lastly, a balance value contains a series of amounts, each with a
different commodity.  Unlike the name, such a value does need to
balance.  It is called a balance because it sums several amounts.  For
example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&lt;value type=&quot;balance&quot;&gt;
  &lt;balance&gt;
    &lt;amount&gt;
      &lt;commodity flags=&quot;PT&quot;&gt;$&lt;/commodity&gt;
      &lt;quantity&gt;90.00&lt;/quantity&gt;
    &lt;/amount&gt;
    &lt;amount&gt;
      &lt;commodity flags=&quot;TE&quot;&gt;DM&lt;/commodity&gt;
      &lt;quantity&gt;200.00&lt;/quantity&gt;
    &lt;/amount&gt;
  &lt;/balance&gt;
&lt;/value&gt;
</pre></div>

<p>That is the extent of the XML data format used by Ledger.  It will
output such data if the <code class="command">xml</code> command is used, and can read
the same data.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="prices-and-pricedb-commands">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#The-xml-command" accesskey="p" rel="prev">The <code class="command">xml</code> command</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports in other Formats</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="prices-and-pricedb-commands-1">7.2.7 <code class="command">prices</code> and <code class="command">pricedb</code> commands</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-prices"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-pricedb"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002daverage"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">prices</code> command displays the price history for matching
commodities.  The <samp class="option">--average (-A)</samp> option is useful with this
report, to display the running average price, or <samp class="option">--deviation
(-D)</samp> to show each price&rsquo;s deviation from that average.
</p>
<p>There is also a <code class="command">pricedb</code> command which outputs the same
information as <code class="command">prices</code>, but does so in a format that can be
parsed by Ledger.  This is useful for generating and tidying up
pricedb database files.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Reports-about-your-Journals">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Reports-in-other-Formats" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Reports in other Formats</a>, Up: <a href="#Reporting-Commands" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reporting Commands</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Reports-about-your-Journals-1">7.3 Reports about your Journals</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dcount"></a>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#accounts" accesskey="1"><code class="command">accounts</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#payees" accesskey="2"><code class="command">payees</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#commodities" accesskey="3"><code class="command">commodities</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#tags" accesskey="4"><code class="command">tags</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#xact" accesskey="5"><code class="command">xact</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#stats" accesskey="6"><code class="command">stats</code></a></li>
<li><a href="#select" accesskey="7"><code class="command">select</code></a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="accounts">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#payees" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">payees</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Reports about your Journals</a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports about your Journals</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="accounts-1">7.3.1 <code class="command">accounts</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-accounts-1"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">accounts</code> command reports all of the accounts in the
journal.  Following the command with a regular expression will limit the
output to accounts matching the regex.  The output is sorted by name.
Using the <samp class="option">--count</samp> option will tell you how many entries use
each account.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="payees">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#commodities" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">commodities</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#accounts" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><code class="command">accounts</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports about your Journals</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="payees-1">7.3.2 <code class="command">payees</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-payees-1"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">payees</code> command reports all of the unique payees in the
journal.  Using the <samp class="option">--count</samp> option will tell you how many
entries use each payee.  To filter the payees displayed you must use the
prefix @:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger payees @Nic
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Nicolas
Nicolas BOILABUS
Oudtshoorn Municipality
Vaca Veronica
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="commodities">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#tags" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">tags</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#payees" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><code class="command">payees</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports about your Journals</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="commodities-1">7.3.3 <code class="command">commodities</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-commodities"></a>

<p>Report all commodities present in the journals under consideration.  The
output is sorted by name.  Using the <samp class="option">--count</samp> option will tell
you how many entries use each commodity.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="tags">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#xact" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">xact</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#commodities" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><code class="command">commodities</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports about your Journals</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="tags-1">7.3.4 <code class="command">tags</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-tags-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dvalues"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">tags</code> command reports all of the tags in the journal.  The
output is sorted by name.  Using the <samp class="option">--count</samp> option will tell
you how many entries use each tag.  Using the <samp class="option">--values</samp> option
will report the values used by each tag.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="xact">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#stats" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">stats</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#tags" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><code class="command">tags</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Reports-about-your-Journals" accesskey="u" rel="up">Reports about your Journals</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="xact-1">7.3.5 <code class="command">xact</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-draft"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-entry"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-xact-1"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">xact</code> command simplifies the creation of new transactions.
It works on the principle that 80% of all postings are variants of
earlier postings.  Here&rsquo;s how it works:
</p>
<p>Say you currently have this posting in your ledger file:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2004/03/15 * Viva Italiano
    Expenses:Food                       $12.45
    Expenses:Tips                        $2.55
    Liabilities:MasterCard             $-15.00
</pre></div>

<p>Now it&rsquo;s &lsquo;<samp class="samp">2004/4/9</samp>&rsquo;, and you&rsquo;ve just eaten at &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Viva Italiano</samp>&rsquo;
again.  The exact amounts are different, but the overall form is the
same.  With the <code class="command">xact</code> command you can type:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger xact 2004/4/9 viva food 11 tips 2.50
</pre></div>

<p>This produces the following output:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2004/04/09 Viva Italiano
    Expenses:Food                             $11.00
    Expenses:Tips                              $2.50
    Liabilities:MasterCard
</pre></div>

<p>It works by finding a past posting matching the regular expression
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">viva</samp>&rsquo;, and assuming that any accounts or amounts specified will be
similar to that earlier posting.  If Ledger does not succeed in
generating a new transaction, an error is printed and the exit code is
set to &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>Here are a few more examples of the <code class="command">xact</code> command, assuming
the above journal transaction:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger xact 4/9 viva 11.50
$ ledger xact 4/9 viva 11.50 checking # (from `checking')
$ ledger xact 4/9 viva food 11.50 tips 8
$ ledger xact 4/9 viva food 11.50 tips 8 cash
$ ledger xact 4/9 viva food $11.50 tips $8 cash
$ ledger xact 4/9 viva dining &quot;DM 11.50&quot;
</pre></div>

<p><code class="command">draft</code> and <code class="command">entry</code> are both synonyms of
<code class="command">xact</code>.  <code class="command">entry</code> is provided for backwards compatibility
with Ledger 2.X.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="stats">
<div class="nav-panel">

</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="stats-1">7.3.6 <code class="command">stats</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-stats"></a>

<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

<h2 class="chapter" id="Command_002dLine-Syntax-1">8 Command-Line Syntax</h2>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Basic-Usage" accesskey="1">Basic Usage</a></li>
<li><a href="#Command_002dLine-Quick-Reference" accesskey="2">Command-Line Quick Reference</a></li>
<li><a href="#Detailed-Option-Description" accesskey="3">Detailed Option Description</a></li>
<li><a href="#Period-Expressions" accesskey="4">Period Expressions</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Basic-Usage">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Quick-Reference" accesskey="n" rel="next">Command-Line Quick Reference</a>, Previous: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Syntax" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Command-Line Syntax</a>, Up: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Syntax" accesskey="u" rel="up">Command-Line Syntax</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Basic-Usage-1">8.1 Basic Usage</h3>

<p>This chapter describes Ledger&rsquo;s features and options.  You may wish to
survey this to get an overview before diving into the <a class="ref" href="#Ledger-Tutorial">Ledger Tutorial</a> and more detailed examples that follow.
</p>
<p>Ledger has a very simple command-line interface, named&mdash;enticingly
enough&mdash;<samp class="file">ledger</samp>.  It supports a few reporting commands, and
a large number of options for refining the output from those commands.
The basic syntax of any ledger command is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger [OPTIONS...] COMMAND [ARGS...]
</pre></div>

<p>After the command word there may appear any number of arguments.  For
most commands, these arguments are regular expressions that cause the
output to relate only to postings matching those regular expressions.
For the <code class="command">xact</code> command, the arguments have a special meaning,
described below.
</p>
<p>The regular expressions arguments always match the account name that
a posting refers to.  To match on the payee of the transaction
instead, precede the regular expression with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">payee</samp>&rsquo; or
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">@</samp>&rsquo;.  For example, the following balance command reports account
totals for rent, food and movies, but only those whose payee matches
Freddie:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger bal rent food movies payee freddie
</pre></div>

<p>or
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger bal rent food movies @freddie
</pre></div>

<p>There are many, many command options available with the <samp class="file">ledger</samp>
program, and it takes a while to master them.  However, none of them are
required to use the basic reporting commands.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Command_002dLine-Quick-Reference">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Detailed-Option-Description" accesskey="n" rel="next">Detailed Option Description</a>, Previous: <a href="#Basic-Usage" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Basic Usage</a>, Up: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Syntax" accesskey="u" rel="up">Command-Line Syntax</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>

<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Basic-Reporting-Commands">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Basic-Options" accesskey="n" rel="next">Basic Options</a>, Previous: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Quick-Reference" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Command-Line Quick Reference</a>, Up: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Quick-Reference" accesskey="u" rel="up">Command-Line Quick Reference</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Basic-Reporting-Commands-1">8.2.1 Basic Reporting Commands</h4>

<dl class="ftable">
<dt id='index-balance-2'><span><code class="command">balance</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-balance-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-bal'><span><code class="command">bal</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-bal'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Show account balances.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-register-6'><span><code class="command">register</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-register-6'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-reg'><span><code class="command">reg</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-reg'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Show all transactions with running total.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-csv-1'><span><code class="command">csv</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-csv-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><a class="index-entry-id" id="index-csv-exporting"></a>
<p>Show transactions in csv format, for exporting to other programs.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-print-4'><span><code class="command">print</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-print-4'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print transactions in a format readable by ledger.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-xml-1'><span><code class="command">xml</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-xml-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Produce XML output of the register command.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-lisp-1'><span><code class="command">lisp</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-lisp-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-emacs-1'><span><code class="command">emacs</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-emacs-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Produce s-expression output, suitable for Emacs.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-equity-2'><span><code class="command">equity</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-equity-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print account balances as transactions.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-prices-1'><span><code class="command">prices</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-prices-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print price history for matching commodities.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-pricedb-1'><span><code class="command">pricedb</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-pricedb-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print price history for matching commodities in a format readable by
ledger.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-xact-2'><span><code class="command">xact</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-xact-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Generate transactions based on previous postings.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Basic-Options">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

<h4 class="subsection" id="Basic-Options-1">8.2.2 Basic Options</h4>

<dl class="ftable">
<dt id='index-_002d_002dhelp'><span><samp class="option">--help</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dhelp'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dh'><span><samp class="option">-h</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dh'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display the man page for <samp class="file">ledger</samp>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dversion'><span><samp class="option">--version</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dversion'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print version information and exit.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dfile-FILE'><span><samp class="option">--file <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dfile-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002df-FILE'><span><samp class="option">-f <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002df-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Read <samp class="file">FILE</samp> as a ledger file.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002doutput-FILE'><span><samp class="option">--output <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002doutput-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002do-FILE'><span><samp class="option">-o <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002do-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Redirect output to <samp class="file">FILE</samp>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dinit_002dfile-FILE'><span><samp class="option">--init-file <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dinit_002dfile-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002di-FILE'><span><samp class="option">-i <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002di-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Specify an options file.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dimport-FILE'><span><samp class="option">--import <var class="var">FILE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dimport-FILE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Import <var class="var">FILE</var> as Python module.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002daccount-STR-1'><span><samp class="option">--account <var class="var">STR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002daccount-STR-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002da-STR'><span><samp class="option">-a <var class="var">STR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002da-STR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Specify default account <var class="var">STR</var> for QIF file postings.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Report-Filtering-1">8.2.3 Report Filtering</h4>

<dl class="ftable">
<dt id='index-_002d_002dcurrent'><span><samp class="option">--current</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dcurrent'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dc'><span><samp class="option">-c</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dc'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display only transactions on or before the current date.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dbegin-DATE'><span><samp class="option">--begin <var class="var">DATE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dbegin-DATE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002db-DATE'><span><samp class="option">-b <var class="var">DATE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002db-DATE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Limit the processing to transactions on or after <var class="var">DATE</var>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dend-DATE'><span><samp class="option">--end <var class="var">DATE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dend-DATE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002de-DATE'><span><samp class="option">-e <var class="var">DATE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002de-DATE'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Limit the processing to transactions before <var class="var">DATE</var>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dperiod-PERIOD_005fEXPRESSION'><span><samp class="option">--period <var class="var">PERIOD_EXPRESSION</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dperiod-PERIOD_005fEXPRESSION'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dp-PERIOD_005fEXPRESSION'><span><samp class="option">-p <var class="var">PERIOD_EXPRESSION</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dp-PERIOD_005fEXPRESSION'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Limit the processing to transactions in <var class="var">PERIOD_EXPRESSION</var> (see <a class="ref" href="#Period-Expressions">Period Expressions</a>).
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dperiod_002dsort-VEXPR-1'><span><samp class="option">--period-sort <var class="var">VEXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dperiod_002dsort-VEXPR-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Sort postings within each period according to <var class="var">VEXPR</var>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dcleared-1'><span><samp class="option">--cleared</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dcleared-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dC'><span><samp class="option">-C</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dC'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display only cleared postings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002ddc'><span><samp class="option">--dc</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002ddc'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display register or balance in debit/credit format.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002duncleared-1'><span><samp class="option">--uncleared</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002duncleared-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dU'><span><samp class="option">-U</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dU'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display only uncleared postings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dreal-2'><span><samp class="option">--real</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dreal-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dR'><span><samp class="option">-R</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display only real postings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dactual'><span><samp class="option">--actual</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dactual'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dL'><span><samp class="option">-L</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dL'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display only actual postings, not automated ones.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002drelated-1'><span><samp class="option">--related</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002drelated-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dr'><span><samp class="option">-r</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dr'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display related postings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dbudget-1'><span><samp class="option">--budget</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dbudget-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Display how close your postings meet your budget.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dadd_002dbudget'><span><samp class="option">--add-budget</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dadd_002dbudget'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Show unbudgeted postings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dunbudgeted'><span><samp class="option">--unbudgeted</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dunbudgeted'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Show only unbudgeted postings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dforecast_002dwhile-VEXPR'><span><samp class="option">--forecast-while <var class="var">VEXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dforecast_002dwhile-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dforecast-VEXPR'><span><samp class="option">--forecast <var class="var">VEXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dforecast-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Project balances into the future.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dlimit-EXPR-2'><span><samp class="option">--limit <var class="var">EXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dlimit-EXPR-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dl-EXPR'><span><samp class="option">-l <var class="var">EXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dl-EXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Limit which postings are used in calculations by <var class="var">EXPR</var>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002damount-EXPR'><span><samp class="option">--amount <var class="var">EXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002damount-EXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dt-EXPR'><span><samp class="option">-t <var class="var">EXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dt-EXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Change value expression reported in <code class="command">register</code> report.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dtotal-VEXPR'><span><samp class="option">--total <var class="var">VEXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dtotal-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dT-VEXPR'><span><samp class="option">-T <var class="var">VEXPR</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dT-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Change the value expression used for &ldquo;totals&rdquo; column in
<code class="command">register</code> and <code class="command">balance</code> reports.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Error-Checking-and-Calculation-Options">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Output-Customization" accesskey="n" rel="next">Output Customization</a>, Previous: <a href="#Report-Filtering" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Report Filtering</a>, Up: <a href="#Command_002dLine-Quick-Reference" accesskey="u" rel="up">Command-Line Quick Reference</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Error-Checking-and-Calculation-Options-1">8.2.4 Error Checking and Calculation Options</h4>

<dl class="ftable">
<dt id='index-_002d_002dstrict-2'><span><samp class="option">--strict</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dstrict-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Accounts, tags or commodities not previously declared will cause
warnings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dpedantic-1'><span><samp class="option">--pedantic</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dpedantic-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Accounts, tags or commodities not previously declared will cause errors.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dcheck_002dpayees'><span><samp class="option">--check-payees</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dcheck_002dpayees'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Enable strict and pedantic checking for payees as well as accounts,
commodities and tags.  This only works in conjunction with
<samp class="option">--strict</samp> or <samp class="option">--pedantic</samp>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dimmediate'><span><samp class="option">--immediate</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dimmediate'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Instruct ledger to evaluate calculations immediately rather than lazily.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>
