<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Operators" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Operators</a>, Up: <a href="#Value-Expressions" accesskey="u" rel="up">Value Expressions</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>

<h3 class="section" id="Complex-expressions-1">11.4 Complex expressions</h3>

<p>More complicated expressions are possible using:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">expr &quot;amount == COMMODITY AMOUNT&quot;</code></dt>
<dd><p>The amount can be any kind of amount supported by ledger,
with or without a commodity.  Use this for decimal values.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">/REGEX/</code></dt>
<dt><code class="code">expr account =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches against an account&rsquo;s full name.  If
a posting, this will match against the account affected by the
posting.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">@/REGEX/</code></dt>
<dt><code class="code">expr payee =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches against a transaction&rsquo;s payee name.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%/REGEX/</code></dt>
<dt><code class="code">expr has_tag(/REGEX/)</code></dt>
<dt><code class="code">expr has_tag('TAG')</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression (REGEX) or string (TAG) that checks for the tags of
a transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr has_meta(/REGEX/)</code></dt>
<dt><code class="code">expr has_meta('TAG')</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression (REGEX) or string (TAG) that checks for the metadata
key of a transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr tag(REGEX) =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches a transaction&rsquo;s tags against its values.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr date =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>Useful for specifying a date in plain terms.  For example, you could say
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">expr date =~ /2014/</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr comment =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches against a posting&rsquo;s comment
field.  This searches only a posting&rsquo;s field, not the transaction&rsquo;s note
or comment field.  For example, <code class="code">ledger reg &quot;expr&quot; &quot;comment =~
/landline/&quot;</code> will match:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014/1/29  Phone bill
    Assets:Checking                           $50.00
    Expenses:Phone                           $-50.00  ; landline bill
</pre></div>

<p>but will not match:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014/1/29  Phone bill  ; landline bill
    ; landline bill
    Assets:Checking                           $50.00
    Expenses:Phone                           $-50.00
</pre></div>

<p>To match the latter, use &lsquo;<samp class="samp">ledger reg &quot;expr&quot; &quot;note =~ /landline/&quot;</samp>&rsquo;
instead.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr note =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches against a transaction&rsquo;s note field.
This searches all comments in the transaction, including comments on
individual postings.  Thus, &lsquo;<samp class="samp">ledger reg &quot;expr&quot; &quot;note =~ /landline/&quot;</samp>&rsquo;
will match all the three examples below:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014/1/29  Phone bill
    Assets:Checking                           $50.00
    Expenses:Phone                           $-50.00  ; landline bill
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014/1/29  Phone bill  ; landline bill
    Assets:Checking                           $50.00
    Expenses:Phone                           $-50.00
</pre></div>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014/1/29  Phone bill
    ; landline bill
    Assets:Checking                           $50.00
    Expenses:Phone                           $-50.00
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">(EXPR)</code></dt>
<dd><p>A sub-expression is nested in parenthesis.  This can be useful passing
more complicated arguments to functions, or for overriding the natural
precedence order of operators.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr base =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches against an account&rsquo;s base name.  If
a posting, this will match against the account affected by the
posting.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr code =~ /REGEX/</code></dt>
<dd><p>A regular expression that matches against the transaction code (the
text that occurs between parentheses before the payee).
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr any(KEYWORD =~ /REGEX/)</code></dt>
<dd><p>The <code class="command">any</code> keyword is used to specify that at least one posting of
the transaction must match the expression in brackets.  For example,
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">ledger -f d reg expr &quot;any(account =~ /Assets:/)&quot;</samp>&rsquo; can be used to
display all transactions which involve at least one &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Assets:</samp>&rsquo;
account.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">expr all(KEYWORD =~ /REGEX/)</code></dt>
<dd><p>The <code class="command">all</code> keyword is used to specify that all postings of a
transactions must match the expression in brackets.  For example,
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">ledger -f d reg expr &quot;all(account =~ /Assets:/)&quot;</samp>&rsquo; can be used to
display all transactions where all accounts are &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Assets:</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>The <code class="command">query</code> command can be used to see how Ledger interprets
your query.  This can be useful if you are not getting the results you
expect (see <a class="pxref" href="#Pre_002dCommands">Pre-Commands</a>).
</p>

<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

<h4 class="subsection" id="Miscellaneous-1">11.4.1 Miscellaneous</h4>

<p>The following Ledger journal data (saved as <samp class="file">expr.dat</samp>) is used to explain the behaviour of the
functions and variables below:
<a class="anchor" id="expr_002edat"></a></p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2015/01/16 * (C0D3) Payee
  Assets:Cash                 Â¤ -123,45
    ; Payee: PiggyBank
  Expenses:Office Supplies
</pre></div>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-abs"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">abs</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-abs'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt class="deffnx defunx-alias-deffnx def-cmd-deffn" id="index-U"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">U</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-U'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the absolute value of the given <var class="var">value</var>, e.g. <var class="var">amount</var>.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(account) %(abs(amount))\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Assets:Cash Â¤ 123,45
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-amount_005fexpr"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">amount_expr</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-amount_005fexpr'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the calculated amount of the posting according to the <samp class="option">--amount</samp>
option.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-ansify_005fif"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">ansify_if</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value color bool</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-ansify_005fif'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Render the given <var class="var">expression</var> as a string, applying the proper ANSI escape
codes to display it in the given <var class="var">color</var> if <var class="var">bool</var> is true.  It
typically checks the value of the option <samp class="option">--color</samp>.  Since ANSI escape
codes include non-printable character sequences, such as escape <kbd class="kbd">^[</kbd>
the following example may not appear as the final result on the command-line.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(ansify_if(account, blue, options.color))\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">[34mAssets:Cash[0m
[34mExpenses:Office Supplies[0m
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-ceiling"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">ceiling</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-ceiling'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the next integer of <var class="var">value</var> toward <em class="math">+</em>infinity.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(account) %(ceiling(amount))\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Assets:Cash Â¤ -123,00
Expenses:Office Supplies Â¤ 124,00
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-code"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">code</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-code'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the transaction code, the string between the parenthesis after the date.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(account) %(code)\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Assets:Cash C0D3
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-commodity-2"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">commodity</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-commodity-2'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the commodity of the posting amount.
</p></dd></dl>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(account) %(commodity)\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Assets:Cash Â¤
Expenses:Office Supplies Â¤
</pre></div>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-date"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">date</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-date'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt class="defvrx defvarx-alias-defvrx def-cmd-defvr" id="index-d"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">d</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-d'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the date of the posting.
</p></dd></dl>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(date) %(account)\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2015/01/16 Assets:Cash
</pre></div>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-display_005famount"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">display_amount</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-display_005famount'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt class="defvrx defvarx-alias-defvrx def-cmd-defvr" id="index-t"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">t</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-t'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p><small class="sc">UNDOCUMENTED</small>! Please help by contributing documentation for this feature.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-display_005ftotal-1"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">display_total</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-display_005ftotal-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt class="defvrx defvarx-alias-defvrx def-cmd-defvr" id="index-T"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">T</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-T'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p><small class="sc">UNDOCUMENTED</small>! Please help by contributing documentation for this feature.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-floor"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">floor</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-floor'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the next integer of <var class="var">value</var> toward <em class="math">-</em>infinity.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(account) %(floor(amount))\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Assets:Cash Â¤ -124,00
Expenses:Office Supplies Â¤ 123,00
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-format"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">format</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">string</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-format'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Evaluate <var class="var">string</var> as format just like the <samp class="option">--format</samp> option.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-format_005fdate"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">format_date</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">date format</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-format_005fdate'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the <var class="var">date</var> as a string using <var class="var">format</var>.  See
<code class="code">strftime (3)</code> for format string details.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(format_date(date, '%A, %B %d. %Y'))\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Friday, January 16. 2015
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-format_005fdatetime"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">format_datetime</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">datetime format</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-format_005fdatetime'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the <var class="var">datetime</var> as a string using <var class="var">format</var>.  Refer to
<code class="code">strftime (3)</code> for format string details.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-get_005fat"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">get_at</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">sequence index</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-get_005fat'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the value in <var class="var">sequence</var> at <var class="var">index</var>.  The first element is <var class="var">index</var> 0.
For internal use only.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-is_005fseq"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">is_seq</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-is_005fseq'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return true if <var class="var">value</var> is a sequence.  For internal use only.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-join"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">join</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-join'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Replace all newlines in <var class="var">value</var> with <code class="code">\n</code>.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-justify"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">justify</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value first_width latter_width right_justify colorize</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-justify'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Right or left justify the string representing <var class="var">value</var>.  The width
of the field in the first line is given by <var class="var">first_width</var>.  For
subsequent lines the width is given by <var class="var">latter_width</var>.  If
<var class="var">latter_width=-1</var>, then <var class="var">first_width</var> is used for all lines.
If <var class="var">right_justify=true</var> then the field is right justified within
the width of the field.  If it is <var class="var">false</var>, then the field is left
justified and padded to the full width of the field.  If
<var class="var">colorize</var> is true, then ledger will honor color settings.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;Â»%(justify(account, 30, 30, true))Â«\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Â»                   Assets:CashÂ«
Â»      Expenses:Office SuppliesÂ«
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-market"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">market</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value datetime</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-market'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt class="deffnx defunx-alias-deffnx def-cmd-deffn" id="index-P-1"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">P</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-P-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the price of <var class="var">value</var> at <var class="var">datetime</var>.  Note that <var class="var">datetime</var>
must be surrounded by brackets in order to be parsed correctly,
e.g. <code class="code">[2012/03/23]</code>.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-nail_005fdown"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">nail_down</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-nail_005fdown'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p><small class="sc">UNDOCUMENTED</small>! Please help by contributing documentation for this feature.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-now"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">now</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-now'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt class="defvrx defvarx-alias-defvrx def-cmd-defvr" id="index-m"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">m</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-m'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the current datetime.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-defvr first-defvar-alias-first-defvr">
<dt class="defvr defvar-alias-defvr" id="index-options"><span class="category-def">Variable: </span><span><strong class="def-name">options</strong><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-options'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>A variable that allows access to the values of the given command-line options
using the long option names, e.g. to see whether <samp class="option">--daily</samp> or <samp class="option">-D</samp>
was given use <code class="code">option.daily</code>.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat -X $ -D --format &quot;%(options.daily) %(options.exchange)\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">true $
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-percent"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">percent</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value_a value_b</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-percent'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Return the percentage of <var class="var">value_a</var> in relation to <var class="var">value_b</var> (used as 100%)
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(percent(amount, 200))\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">-61.73%
61.73%
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-print-5"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">print</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">value</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-print-5'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print <var class="var">value</var> to stdout.  For internal use only.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">

<dd><p>Return the quantity of <var class="var">value</var> for values that have a per-unit cost.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-quoted"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">quoted</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">expression</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-quoted'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Surround <var class="var">expression</var> with double quotes.  If expression contains
a double quote, it will be escaped with a backslash.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%(quoted(account)) %(quoted(amount))\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&quot;Assets:Cash&quot; &quot;Â¤ -123,45&quot;
&quot;Expenses:Office Supplies&quot; &quot;Â¤ 123,45&quot;
</pre></div>
</dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">
<dt class="deffn defun-alias-deffn" id="index-quoted_005frfc"><span class="category-def">Function: </span><span><strong class="def-name">quoted_rfc</strong> <var class="def-var-arguments">expression</var><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-quoted_005frfc'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Similar, except an embedded double quote would be escaped by
preceding it with another double quote, as prescribed by RFC 4180.
</p></dd></dl>

<dl class="first-deffn first-defun-alias-first-deffn">

</p></dd></dl>

<h2 class="chapter" id="Format-Strings-1">12 Format Strings</h2>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Format-String-Basics" accesskey="1">Format String Basics</a></li>

</ul>
<hr>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Format-String-Basics">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Format-String-Structure" accesskey="n" rel="next">Format String Structure</a>, Previous: <a href="#Format-Strings" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Format Strings</a>, Up: <a href="#Format-Strings" accesskey="u" rel="up">Format Strings</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Format-String-Basics-1">12.1 Format String Basics</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-3"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dbalance_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-3"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dbudget_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-1"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dcleared_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-2"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dcsv_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-2"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dplot_002damount_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-3"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dplot_002dtotal_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-3"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dpricedb_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-2"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dprices_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-3"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dregister_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-3"></a>

<p>Format strings may be used to change the output format of reports.  They
are specified by passing a formatting string to the <samp class="option">--format
<var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var> (-F)</samp> option.  Within that string, constructs are
allowed which make it possible to display the various parts of an
account or posting in custom ways.
</p>
<p>There are several additional flags that allow you to define formats
for specific reports.  These are useful to define in your configuration
file and will allow you to run ledger reports from the command-line
without having to enter a new format for each command.
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li><samp class="option">--balance-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--budget-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--cleared-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--csv-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--plot-amount-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--plot-total-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--pricedb-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--prices-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li><li><samp class="option">--register-format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
</li></ul>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Format-String-Structure">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Format-Expressions" accesskey="n" rel="next">Format Expressions</a>, Previous: <a href="#Format-String-Basics" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Format String Basics</a>, Up: <a href="#Format-Strings" accesskey="u" rel="up">Format Strings</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Format-String-Structure-1">12.2 Format String Structure</h3>

<p>Within a format string, a substitution is specified using a percent
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">%</samp>&rsquo; character.  The basic format of all substitutions is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">%[-][MIN WIDTH][.MAX WIDTH](VALEXPR)
</pre></div>

<p>If the optional minus sign &lsquo;<samp class="samp">-</samp>&rsquo; follows the percent character
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">%</samp>&rsquo;, whatever is substituted will be left justified.  The default
is right justified.  If a minimum width is given next, the substituted
text will be at least that wide, perhaps wider.  If a period and
a maximum width is given, the substituted text will never be wider
than this, and will be truncated to fit.  Here are some examples:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%-20P</code></dt>
<dd><p>A transaction&rsquo;s payee, left justified and padded to 20 characters wide.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%20P</code></dt>
<dd><p>The same, right justified, at least 20 chars wide.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%.20P</code></dt>
<dd><p>The same, no more than 20 chars wide.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>The expression following the format constraints can be a single letter,
or an expression enclosed in parentheses or brackets.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Format-Expressions">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Balance-format" accesskey="n" rel="next">Balance format</a>, Previous: <a href="#Format-String-Structure" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Format String Structure</a>, Up: <a href="#Format-Strings" accesskey="u" rel="up">Format Strings</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Format-Expressions-1">12.3 Format Expressions</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002damount-EXPR-4"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dtotal-VEXPR-4"></a>

<p>For demonstration purposes the journal data from <a class="ref" href="#expr_002edat">expr.dat</a> is used.
The allowable expressions are:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts a percent sign.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%%\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">%
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">t</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the results of the value expression specified by
<samp class="option">--amount <var class="var">EXPR</var> (-t)</samp>.  If <samp class="option">--amount <var class="var">EXPR</var> (-t)</samp>
was not specified, the current report style&rsquo;s value expression is used.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">T</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the results of the value expression specified by <samp class="option">--total
<var class="var">VEXPR</var> (-T)</samp>.  If <samp class="option">--total <var class="var">VEXPR</var> (-T)</samp> was not
specified, the current report style&rsquo;s value expression is used.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">(EXPR)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the amount resulting from the value expression given in
parentheses.  To insert five times the total value of an account, for
example, one could say &lsquo;<samp class="samp">%12(5*O)</samp>&rsquo;.  Note: It&rsquo;s important to put the
five first in that expression, so that the commodity doesn&rsquo;t get
stripped from the total.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%12(5*O)\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">   Â¤ -617,25
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">[DATEFMT]</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the result of formatting a posting&rsquo;s date with a date format
string, exactly like those supported by <code class="code">strftime (3)</code>.  For
example: &lsquo;<samp class="samp">%[%Y/%m/%d %H:%M:%S]</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">S</code></dt>
<dd><p>Insert the path name of the file from which the transaction&rsquo;s data was
read.  Only sensible in a <code class="command">register</code> report.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f ~/journal.dat --format &quot;%S\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">/home/jwiegley/journal.dat
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">B</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the beginning character position of that transaction within the
file.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%B\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">26
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">b</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the beginning line of that transaction within the file.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%b\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">E</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the ending character position of that transaction within the
file.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%E\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">90
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">e</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the ending line of that transaction within the file.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%e\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">3
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">D</code></dt>
<dd><p>Returns the date according to the default format.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">d</code></dt>
<dd><p>Returns the date according to the default format.  If the transaction
has an effective date, it prints <code class="code">ACTUAL_DATE=EFFECTIVE_DATE</code>.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">X</code></dt>
<dd><p>If a posting has been cleared, this returns a 1, otherwise returns 0.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">Y</code></dt>
<dd><p>This is the same as &lsquo;<samp class="samp">%X</samp>&rsquo;, except that it only displays a state
character if all of the member postings have the same state.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">C</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the transaction code.  This is the value specified between
parentheses on the first line of the transaction.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%C\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">(C0D3) 
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">P</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the payee related to a posting.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%P\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">PiggyBank
</pre></div>


</dd>
<dt><code class="code">A</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the full name of an account.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%A\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">Assets:Cash
Expenses:Office Supplies
</pre></div>



</dd>
<dt><code class="code">N</code></dt>
<dd><p>Inserts the note associated with a posting, if one exists.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%N\n&quot; reg assets
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted"> Payee: PiggyBank
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt><code class="code">/</code></dt>
<dd><p>The &lsquo;<samp class="samp">%/</samp>&rsquo; construct is special.  It separates a format string
between what is printed for the first posting of a transaction, and
what is printed for all subsequent postings.  If not used, the
same format string is used for all postings.
</p><div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger -f expr.dat --format &quot;%P\n%/%A\n&quot; reg
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">PiggyBank
Expenses:Office Supplies
</pre></div>

</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Balance-format">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="n" rel="next">Formatting Functions and Codes</a>, Previous: <a href="#Format-Expressions" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Format Expressions</a>, Up: <a href="#Format-Strings" accesskey="u" rel="up">Format Strings</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Balance-format-1">12.4 Balance format</h3>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dbalance_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-4"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dformat-FORMAT_005fSTRING-4"></a>

<p>As an example of how flexible the <samp class="option">--format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></samp>
strings can be, the default balance format looks like this (the various
functions are described later):
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">&quot;%(justify(scrub(display_total), 20, -1, true, color))&quot;
&quot;  %(!options.flat ? depth_spacer : \&quot;\&quot;)&quot;
&quot;%-(ansify_if(partial_account(options.flat), blue if color))\n%/&quot;
&quot;%$1\n%/&quot;
&quot;--------------------\n&quot;
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>

<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Field-Widths">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Colors" accesskey="n" rel="next">Colors</a>, Previous: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Formatting Functions and Codes</a>, Up: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Formatting Functions and Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>

<h4 class="subsection" id="Field-Widths-1">12.5.1 Field Widths</h4>

<p>The following codes return the width allocated for the specific fields.
The defaults can be changed using the corresponding command-line
options:
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li><code class="code">date_width</code>
</li><li><code class="code">payee_width</code>
</li><li><code class="code">account_width</code>
</li><li><code class="code">amount_width</code>
</li><li><code class="code">total_width</code>
</li></ul>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Colors">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

<h4 class="subsection" id="Colors-1">12.5.2 Colors</h4>

<p>The character-based formatting ledger can do is limited to the ANSI
terminal character colors and font highlights in a normal TTY session.
</p>
<table class="multitable">
<tbody><tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">red</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">magenta</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">bold</code></td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">green</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">cyan</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">underline</code></td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">yellow</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">white</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">blink</code></td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">blue</code></td><td width="30%"><code class="code">black</code></td></tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Date-Functions">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="n" rel="next">Date and Time Format Codes</a>, Previous: <a href="#Quantities-and-Calculations" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Quantities and Calculations</a>, Up: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Formatting Functions and Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Date-Functions-1">12.5.4 Date Functions</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dnow-DATE-2"></a>

<p>The following functions allow you to manipulate and format dates.
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">date</code></dt>
<dd><p>Return the date of the current transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">format_date(date, &quot;FORMAT_STRING&quot;)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Format the date using the given format string.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">now</code></dt>
<dd><p>Return the current date and time.  If the <samp class="option">--now <var class="var">DATE</var></samp>
option is defined it will return that value.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">today</code></dt>
<dd><p>Return the current date.  If the <samp class="option">--now <var class="var">DATE</var></samp> option is
defined it will return that value.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">to_datetime</code></dt>
<dd><p>Convert a string to a date-time value.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">to_date</code></dt>
<dd><p>Convert a string to date value.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">value_date</code></dt>
</dl>


<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Date-and-Time-Format-Codes">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Text-Formatting" accesskey="n" rel="next">Text Formatting</a>, Previous: <a href="#Date-Functions" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Date Functions</a>, Up: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Formatting Functions and Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Date-and-Time-Format-Codes-1">12.5.5 Date and Time Format Codes</h4>

<p>Date and time format are specified as strings of single letter codes
preceded by percent signs.  Any separator, or no separator can be
specified.
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Days" accesskey="1">Days</a></li>
<li><a href="#Weekdays" accesskey="2">Weekdays</a></li>
<li><a href="#Month" accesskey="3">Month</a></li>
<li><a href="#Miscellaneous-Date-Codes" accesskey="4">Miscellaneous Date Codes</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Days">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Weekdays" accesskey="n" rel="next">Weekdays</a>, Previous: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Date and Time Format Codes</a>, Up: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Date and Time Format Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Days-1">12.5.5.1 Days</h4>

<p>Dates are formed from a combination of day, month and year codes, in
whatever order you prefer:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%Y</code></dt>
<dd><p>Four digit year.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%y</code></dt>
<dd><p>Two digit year.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%m</code></dt>
<dd><p>Two digit month.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%d</code></dt>
<dd><p>Two digit date.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>So <code class="code">&quot;%Y%m%d&quot;</code> yields &lsquo;<samp class="samp">20111214</samp>&rsquo; which provides a date that
is simple to sort on.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Weekdays">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Month" accesskey="n" rel="next">Month</a>, Previous: <a href="#Days" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Days</a>, Up: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Date and Time Format Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Weekdays-1">12.5.5.2 Weekdays</h4>

<p>You can have additional weekday information in your date with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">%A</samp>&rsquo;
as
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%m-%d-%Y %A</code></dt>
<dd><p>yields &lsquo;<samp class="samp">02-10-2010 Wednesday</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%A %m-%d-%Y</code></dt>
<dd><p>yields &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Wednesday 02-10-2010</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>These are options you can select for weekday
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%a</code></dt>
<dd><p>weekday, abbreviated Wed.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%A</code></dt>
<dd><p>weekday, full Wednesday.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%d</code></dt>
<dd><p>day of the month (dd), zero padded up to 10.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%e</code></dt>
<dd><p>day of the month (dd), no leading zero up to 10.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%j</code></dt>
<dd><p>day of year, zero padded 000&ndash;366.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%u</code></dt>
<dd><p>day of week starting with Monday (1), i.e. <code class="code">mtwtfss</code> 3.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%w</code></dt>
<dd><p>day of week starting with Sunday (0), i.e. <code class="code">smtwtfs</code> 3.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Month">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Miscellaneous-Date-Codes" accesskey="n" rel="next">Miscellaneous Date Codes</a>, Previous: <a href="#Weekdays" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Weekdays</a>, Up: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Date and Time Format Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Month-1">12.5.5.3 Month</h4>

<p>You can have additional month information in your date with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">%B</samp>&rsquo;
as
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%m-%d-%Y %B</code></dt>
<dd><p>yields &lsquo;<samp class="samp">02-10-2010 February</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%B %m-%d-%Y</code></dt>
<dd><p>yields &lsquo;<samp class="samp">February 02-10-2010</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<p>These are options you can select for month
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%m</code></dt>
<dd><p>&lsquo;<samp class="samp">mm</samp>&rsquo; month as two digits.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%b</code></dt>
<dd><p>Localeâs abbreviated month, for example &lsquo;<samp class="samp">02</samp>&rsquo; might be abbreviated
as &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Feb</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%B</code></dt>
<dd><p>Localeâs full month, variable length, e.g. February.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Miscellaneous-Date-Codes">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Month" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Month</a>, Up: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Date and Time Format Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Miscellaneous-Date-Codes-1">12.5.5.4 Miscellaneous Date Codes</h4>

<p>Additional date format parameters which can be used:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">%U</code></dt>
<dd><p>week number Sunday as first day of week, ranging 01&ndash;53.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%W</code></dt>
<dd><p>week number Monday as first day of week, ranging 01&ndash;53.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%V</code></dt>
<dd><p>week of the year, ranging 01&ndash;53.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%C</code></dt>
<dd><p>century, ranging 00&ndash;99.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%D</code></dt>
<dd><p>yields <code class="code">%m/%d/%y</code> as in &lsquo;<samp class="samp">02/10/10</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%x</code></dt>
<dd><p>localeâs date representation, as &lsquo;<samp class="samp">02/10/2010</samp>&rsquo; for the U.S.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">%F</code></dt>
<dd><p>yields <code class="code">%Y-%m-%d</code> as in &lsquo;<samp class="samp">2010-02-10</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Text-Formatting">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Data-File-Parsing-Information" accesskey="n" rel="next">Data File Parsing Information</a>, Previous: <a href="#Date-and-Time-Format-Codes" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Date and Time Format Codes</a>, Up: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Formatting Functions and Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Text-Formatting-1">12.5.6 Text Formatting</h4>

<p>The following format functions allow you limited formatting of text:
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">ansify_if(value, color)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Surrounds the string representing value with ANSI codes to give it
<code class="code">color</code> on a TTY display.  Has no effect if directed to a file.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">justify(value, first_width, latter_width, right_justify, colorize)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Right or left justify the string representing <code class="code">value</code>.  The width
of the field in the first line is given by <code class="code">first_width</code>.  For
subsequent lines the width is given by <code class="code">latter_width</code>.  If
<code class="code">latter_width=-1</code>, then <code class="code">first_width</code> is use for all lines.
If <code class="code">right_justify=true</code> then the field is right justify within
the width of the field.  If it is <code class="code">false</code>, then the field is left
justified and padded to the full width of the field.  If
<code class="code">colorize</code> is true, then ledger will honor color settings.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">join(STR)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Replaces line feeds in <code class="code">STR</code> with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">\n</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">quoted(STR)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Return <code class="code">STR</code> surrounded by double quotes, &lsquo;<samp class="samp">&quot;STR&quot;</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">strip(value)</code></dt>
<dd><p>Values can have numerous annotations, such as effective dates and lot
prices.  <code class="code">strip</code> removes these annotations.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Data-File-Parsing-Information">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Text-Formatting" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Text Formatting</a>, Up: <a href="#Formatting-Functions-and-Codes" accesskey="u" rel="up">Formatting Functions and Codes</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Data-File-Parsing-Information-1">12.5.7 Data File Parsing Information</h4>

<p>The following format strings provide locational metadata
regarding the coordinates of entries in the source data file(s) that
generated the posting.
</p>
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">filename</code></dt>
<dd><p>the name of the ledger data file from whence the posting came,
abbreviated &lsquo;<samp class="samp">S</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">beg_pos</code></dt>
<dd><p>character position in <code class="code">filename</code> where entry for posting begins,
abbreviated &lsquo;<samp class="samp">B</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">end_pos</code></dt>
<dd><p>character position in <code class="code">filename</code> where entry for posting ends,
abbreviated &lsquo;<samp class="samp">E</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">beg_line</code></dt>
<dd><p>line number in <code class="code">filename</code> where entry for posting begins,
abbreviated &lsquo;<samp class="samp">b</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
<dt><code class="code">end_line</code></dt>
<dd><p>line number in <code class="code">filename</code> where entry for posting ends,
abbreviated &lsquo;<samp class="samp">e</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="chapter-level-extent" id="Extending-with-Python">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Ledger-for-Developers" accesskey="n" rel="next">Ledger for Developers</a>, Previous: <a href="#Format-Strings" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Format Strings</a>, Up: <a href="#Top" accesskey="u" rel="up">Overview</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h2 class="chapter" id="Extending-with-Python-1">13 Extending with Python</h2>

<p>Python can be used to extend your Ledger experience.  But first,
a word must be said about Ledger&rsquo;s data model, so that other things
make sense later.
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Basic-data-traversal" accesskey="1">Basic data traversal</a></li>
<li><a href="#Raw-versus-Cooked" accesskey="2">Raw versus Cooked</a></li>
<li><a href="#Queries" accesskey="3">Queries</a></li>
<li><a href="#Embedded-Python" accesskey="4">Embedded Python</a></li>
<li><a href="#Amounts" accesskey="5">Amounts</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Basic-data-traversal">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Raw-versus-Cooked" accesskey="n" rel="next">Raw versus Cooked</a>, Previous: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Extending with Python</a>, Up: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="u" rel="up">Extending with Python</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Basic-data-traversal-1">13.1 Basic data traversal</h3>

<p>Every interaction with Ledger happens in the context of a Session.
Even if you don&rsquo;t create a session manually, one is created for you by
the top-level interface functions.  The Session is where objects live
like the Commodities that Amounts refer to.
</p>
<p>To make a Session useful, you must read a Journal into it, using the
function &lsquo;<code class="code">read_journal</code>&lsquo;.  This reads Ledger data from the given
file, populates a Journal object within the current Session, and
returns a reference to that Journal object.
</p>
<p>Within the Journal live all the Transactions, Postings, and other
objects related to your data.  There are also AutomatedTransactions
and PeriodicTransactions, etc.
</p>
<p>Here is how you would traverse all the postings in your data file:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">import ledger

for xact in ledger.read_journal(&quot;sample.dat&quot;).xacts():
    for post in xact.posts():
        print &quot;Transferring %s to/from %s&quot; % (post.amount, post.account)
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Raw-versus-Cooked">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Queries" accesskey="n" rel="next">Queries</a>, Previous: <a href="#Basic-data-traversal" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Basic data traversal</a>, Up: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="u" rel="up">Extending with Python</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Raw-versus-Cooked-1">13.2 Raw versus Cooked</h3>

<p>Ledger data exists in one of two forms: raw and cooked.  Raw objects are
what you get from a traversal like the above, and represent exactly what
was seen in the data file.  Consider this journal:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">= true
    (Assets:Cash)    $100

2012-03-01 KFC
    Expenses:Food    $100
    Assets:Credit
</pre></div>

<p>In this case, the <em class="emph">raw</em> regular transaction in this file is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2012-03-01 KFC
    Expenses:Food    $100
    Assets:Credit
</pre></div>

<p>While the <em class="emph">cooked</em> form is:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2012-03-01 KFC
    Expenses:Food    $100
    Assets:Credit   $-100
    (Assets:Cash)    $100
</pre></div>

<p>So the easy way to think about raw vs. cooked is that raw is the
unprocessed data, and cooked has had all considerations applied.
</p>
<p>When you traverse a Journal by iterating over its transactions, you are
generally looking at raw data.  In order to look at cooked data, you
must generate a report of some kind by querying the journal:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">for post in ledger.read_journal(&quot;sample.dat&quot;).query(&quot;food&quot;):
    print &quot;Transferring %s to/from %s&quot; % (post.amount, post.account)
</pre></div>

<p>The reason why queries iterate over postings instead of transactions is
that queries often return only a &ldquo;slice&rdquo; of the transactions they
apply to.  You can always get at a matching posting&rsquo;s transaction by
looking at its <code class="code">xact</code> member:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">last_xact = None
for post in ledger.read_journal(&quot;sample.dat&quot;).query(&quot;&quot;):
    if post.xact != last_xact:
        for post in post.xact.posts():
            print &quot;Transferring %s to/from %s&quot; % (post.amount,
            post.account)
        last_xact = post.xact
</pre></div>

<p>This query ends up reporting every cooked posting in the Journal, but
does it transaction-wise.  It relies on the fact that an unsorted report
returns postings in the exact order they were parsed from the journal
file.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Queries">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Embedded-Python" accesskey="n" rel="next">Embedded Python</a>, Previous: <a href="#Raw-versus-Cooked" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Raw versus Cooked</a>, Up: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="u" rel="up">Extending with Python</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Queries-1">13.3 Queries</h3>

<p>The Journal.query() method accepts every argument you can specify on the
command-line, including <samp class="option">--options</samp>.
</p>
<p>Since a query &ldquo;cooks&rdquo; the journal it applies to, only one query may be
active for that journal at a given time.  Once the query object is gone
(after the for loop), then the data reverts back to its raw state.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Embedded-Python">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Amounts" accesskey="n" rel="next">Amounts</a>, Previous: <a href="#Queries" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Queries</a>, Up: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="u" rel="up">Extending with Python</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Embedded-Python-1">13.4 Embedded Python</h3>

<p>You can embed Python into your data files using the &rsquo;python&rsquo; directive:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">python
    import os
    def check_path(path_value):
        print &quot;%s =&gt; %s&quot; % (str(path_value), os.path.isfile(str(path_value)))
        return os.path.isfile(str(path_value))

tag PATH
    assert check_path(value)

2012-02-29 KFC
    ; PATH: somebogusfile.dat
    Expenses:Food                $20
    Assets:Cash
</pre></div>

<p>Any Python functions you define this way become immediately available as
valexpr functions.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Amounts">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Embedded-Python" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Embedded Python</a>, Up: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="u" rel="up">Extending with Python</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Amounts-1">13.5 Amounts</h3>

<p>When numbers come from Ledger, like post.amount, the type of the value
is Amount.  It can be used just like an ordinary number, except that
addition and subtraction are restricted to amounts with the same
commodity.  If you need to create sums of multiple commodities, use
a Balance.  For example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">total = Balance()
for post in ledger.read_journal(&quot;sample.dat&quot;).query(&quot;&quot;):
    total += post.amount
print total
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="chapter-level-extent" id="Ledger-for-Developers">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Major-Changes-from-version-2_002e6" accesskey="n" rel="next">Major Changes from version 2.6</a>, Previous: <a href="#Extending-with-Python" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Extending with Python</a>, Up: <a href="#Top" accesskey="u" rel="up">Overview</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h2 class="chapter" id="Ledger-for-Developers-1">14 Ledger for Developers</h2>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Internal-Design" accesskey="1">Internal Design</a></li>
<li><a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="2">Journal File Format for Developers</a></li>
<li><a href="#Developer-Commands" accesskey="3">Developer Commands</a></li>
<li><a href="#Ledger-Development-Environment" accesskey="4">Ledger Development Environment</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Internal-Design">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="n" rel="next">Journal File Format for Developers</a>, Previous: <a href="#Ledger-for-Developers" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Ledger for Developers</a>, Up: <a href="#Ledger-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Ledger for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Internal-Design-1">14.1 Internal Design</h3>

<p>Ledger is developed as a tiered set of functionality, where lower tiers
know nothing about the higher tiers.  In fact, multiple libraries are
built during the development the process, and link unit tests to these
libraries, so that it is a link error for a lower tier to violate this
modularity.
</p>
<p>Those tiers are:
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li>Utility code

<p>There&rsquo;s lots of general utility in Ledger for doing time parsing, using
Boost.Regex, error handling, etc.  It&rsquo;s all done in a way that can be
reused in other projects as needed.
</p>
</li><li>Commoditized Amounts (amount_t, commodity_t and friends)

<p>A numerical abstraction combining multi-precision rational numbers (via
GMP) with commodities.  These structures can be manipulated like regular
numbers in either C++ or Python (as Amount objects).
</p>
</li><li>Commodity Pool

<p>Commodities are all owned by a commodity pool, so that future parsing of
amounts can link to the same commodity and established a consistent
price history and record of formatting details.
</p>
</li><li>Balances

<p>Adds the concept of multiple amounts with varying commodities.  Supports
simple arithmetic, and multiplication and division with non-commoditized
values.
</p>
</li><li>Price history

<p>Amounts have prices, and these are kept in a data graph which the amount
code itself is only dimly aware of (there&rsquo;s three points of access so an
amount can query its revalued price on a given date).
</p>
</li><li>Values

<p>Often the higher layers in Ledger don&rsquo;t care if something is an amount
or a balance, they just want to add stuff to it or print it.  For this,
I created a type-erasure class, value_t/Value, into which many things
can be stuffed and then operated on.  They can contain amounts,
balances, dates, strings, etc.  If you try to apply an operation between
two values that makes no sense (like dividing an amount by a balance),
an error occurs at runtime, rather than at compile-time (as would happen
if you actually tried to divide an <code class="code">amount_t</code> by
a <code class="code">balance_t</code>).
</p>
<p>This is the core data type for the value expression language.
</p>
</li><li>Value expressions

<p>The next layer up adds functions and operators around the Value concept.
This lets you apply transformations and tests to Values at runtime
without having to bake it into C++.  The set of functions available is
defined by each object type in Ledger (posts, accounts, transactions,
etc.), though the core engine knows nothing about these.  At its base,
it only knows how to apply operators to values, and how to pass them to
and receive them from functions.
</p>
</li><li>Query expressions

<p>Expressions can be onerous to type at the command-line, so there&rsquo;s
a shorthand for reporting called &ldquo;query expressions&rdquo;.  These add no
functionality of their own, but are purely translated from the input
string  down to the corresponding value expression, for example the
input string &lsquo;<samp class="samp">cash</samp>&rsquo; is translated to &lsquo;<samp class="samp">(account
=~ /cash/)</samp>&rsquo;.  This is a convenience layer.
</p>
</li><li>Format strings

<p>Format strings let you interpolate value expressions into strings, with
the requirement that any interpolated value have a string
representation.  Really all this does is calculate the value expression
in the current report context, call the resulting value&rsquo;s
<code class="code">to_string()</code> method, and stuffs the result into the output string.
It also provides printf-like behavior, such as min/max width, right/left
justification, etc.
</p>
</li><li>Journal items

<p>Next is a base type shared by anything that can appear in a journal: an
item_t.  It contains details common to all such parsed entities, like
what file and line it was found on, etc.
</p>
</li><li>Journal posts

<p>The most numerous object found in a Journal, postings are a type of item
that contain an account, an amount, a cost, and metadata.  There are
some other complications, like the account can be marked virtual, the
amount could be an expression, etc.
</p>
</li><li>Journal transactions

<p>Postings are owned by transactions, always.  This subclass of <code class="code">item_t</code>
knows about the date, the payee, etc.  If a date or metadata tag is
requested from a posting and it doesn&rsquo;t have that information, the
transaction is queried to see if it can provide it.
</p>
</li><li>Journal accounts

<p>Postings are also shared by accounts, though the actual memory is
managed by the transaction.  Each account knows all the postings within
it, but contains relatively little information of its own.
</p>
</li><li>The Journal object

<p>Finally, all transactions with their postings, and all accounts, are
owned by a <code class="code">journal_t</code> object.  This is the go-to object for
querying and reporting on your data.
</p>
</li><li>Textual journal parser

<p>There is a textual parser, wholly contained in <samp class="file">textual.cc</samp>, which
knows how to parse text into journal objects, which then get
&ldquo;finalized&rdquo; and added to the journal.  Finalization is the step that
enforces the double-entry guarantee.
</p>
</li><li>Iterators

<p>Every journal object is &ldquo;iterable&rdquo;, and these iterators are defined in
<samp class="file">iterators.h</samp> and <samp class="file">iterators.cc</samp>.  This iteration logic is kept out of the
basic journal objects themselves for the sake of modularity.
</p>
</li><li>Comparators

<p>Another abstraction isolated to its own layer, this class encapsulating
the comparison of journal objects, based on whatever value expression
the user passed to <samp class="option">--sort <var class="var">VEXPR</var></samp>.
</p>
</li><li>Temporaries

<p>Many reports bring pseudo-journal objects into existence, like postings
which report totals in a &lsquo;<samp class="samp">Total</samp>&rsquo; account.  These objects are
created and managed by a <code class="code">temporaries_t</code> object, which gets used in
many places by the reporting filters.
</p>
</li><li>Option handling

<p>There is an option handling subsystem used by many of the layers further
down.  It makes it relatively easy for me to add new options, and to
have those option settings immediately accessible to value expressions.
</p>
</li><li>Session objects

<p>Every journal object is owned by a session, with the session providing
support for that object.  In GUI terms, this is the Controller object
for the journal Data object, where every document window would be
a separate session.  They are all owned by the global scope.
</p>
</li><li>Report objects

<p>Every time you create any report output, a report object is created to
determine what you want to see.  In the Ledger REPL, a new report object
is created every time a command is executed.  In CLI mode, only one
report object ever comes into being, as Ledger immediately exits after
displaying the results.
</p>
</li><li>Reporting filters

<p>The way Ledger generates data is this: it asks the session for the
current journal, and then creates an iterator applied to that journal.
The kind of iterator depends on the type of report.
</p>
<p>This iterator is then walked, and every object yielded from the iterator
is passed to an &ldquo;item handler&rdquo;, whose type is directly related to the
type of the iterator.
</p>
<p>There are many, many item handlers, which can be chained together.  Each
one receives an item (post, account, xact, etc.), performs some action
on it, and then passes it down to the next handler in the chain.  There
are filters which compute the running totals; that queue and sort all
the input items before playing them back out in a new order; that filter
out items which fail to match a predicate, etc.  Almost every reporting
feature in Ledger is related to one or more filters.  Looking at
<samp class="file">filters.h</samp>, there are over 25 of them defined currently.
</p>
</li><li>The filter chain

<p>How filters get wired up, and in what order, is a complex process based
on all the various options specified by the user.  This is the job of
the chain logic, found entirely in <samp class="file">chain.cc</samp>.  It took a really
long time to get this logic exactly right, which is why I haven&rsquo;t
exposed this layer to the Python bridge yet.
</p>
</li><li>Output modules

<p>Although filters are great and all, in the end you want to see stuff.
This is the job of special &ldquo;leaf&rdquo; filters called output modules.  They
are implemented just like a regular filter, but they don&rsquo;t have
a &ldquo;next&rdquo; filter to pass the data on down to.  Instead, they are the
end of the line and must do something with the item that results in the
user seeing something on their screen or in a file.
</p>
</li><li>Select queries

<p>Select queries know a lot about everything, even though they implement
their logic by implementing the user&rsquo;s query in terms of all the other
features thus presented.  Select queries have no functionality of their
own, they are simple a shorthand to provide access to much of Ledger&rsquo;s
functionality via a cleaner, more consistent syntax.
</p>
</li><li>The Global Scope

<p>There is a master object which owns every other objects, and this is
Ledger&rsquo;s global scope.  It creates the other objects, provides REPL
behavior for the command-line utility, etc.  In GUI terms, this is the
Application object.
</p>
</li><li>The Main Driver

<p>This creates the global scope object, performs error reporting, and
handles command-line options which must precede even the creation of the
global scope, such as <samp class="option">--debug <var class="var">CODE</var></samp>.
</p>
</li></ul>

<p>And that&rsquo;s Ledger in a nutshell.  All the rest are details, such as
which value expressions each journal item exposes, how many filters
currently exist, which options the report and session scopes define,
etc.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="section-level-extent" id="Journal-File-Format-for-Developers">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Developer-Commands" accesskey="n" rel="next">Developer Commands</a>, Previous: <a href="#Internal-Design" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Internal Design</a>, Up: <a href="#Ledger-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Ledger for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Journal-File-Format-for-Developers-1">14.2 Journal File Format for Developers</h3>

<p>This chapter offers a complete description of the journal data format,
suitable for implementers in other languages to follow.  For users, the
chapter on keeping a journal is less extensive, but more typical of
common usage (see <a class="pxref" href="#Keeping-a-Journal">Keeping a Journal</a>).
</p>
<p>Data is collected in the form of <em class="dfn">transactions</em> which occur in one
or more <em class="dfn">journal files</em>.  Each transaction, in turn, is made up of
one or more <em class="dfn">postings</em>, which describe how <em class="dfn">amounts</em> flow from
one <em class="dfn">account</em> to another.  Here is an example of the simplest of
journal files:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 Just an example
    Expenses:Some:Account                $100.00
    Income:Another:Account
</pre></div>

<p>In this example, there is a transaction date, a payee, or description of
the transaction, and two postings.  The postings show movement of one
hundred dollars from an account within the Income hierarchy, to the
specified expense account.  The name and meaning of these accounts is
arbitrary, with no preferences implied, although you will find it useful
to follow standard accounting practices (see <a class="pxref" href="#Principles-of-Accounting-with-Ledger">Principles of Accounting with Ledger</a>).
</p>
<p>Since an amount is missing from the second posting, it is assumed to be
the inverse of the first.  This guarantees the cardinal rule of
double-entry accounting: the sum of every transaction must balance to
zero, or it is in error.  Whenever Ledger encounters a <em class="dfn">null
posting</em> in a transaction, it uses it to balance the remainder.
</p>
<p>It is also typical, though not enforced, to think of the first posting
as the destination, and the final as the source.  Thus, the amount of
the first posting is typically positive.  Consider:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 An income transaction
    Assets:Checking       $1,000.00
    Income:Salary

2010/05/31 An expense transaction
    Expenses:Dining         $100.00
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Comments-and-meta_002ddata" accesskey="1">Comments and meta-data</a></li>
<li><a href="#Specifying-Amounts" accesskey="2">Specifying Amounts</a></li>
<li><a href="#Posting-costs" accesskey="3">Posting costs</a></li>
<li><a href="#Primary-commodities" accesskey="4">Primary commodities</a></li>
</ul>
