<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Comments-and-meta_002ddata">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Specifying-Amounts" accesskey="n" rel="next">Specifying Amounts</a>, Previous: <a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Journal File Format for Developers</a>, Up: <a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Journal File Format for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Comments-and-meta_002ddata-1">14.2.1 Comments and meta-data</h4>

<p>Comments are generally started using a &lsquo;<samp class="samp">;</samp>&rsquo;.  However, in order to
increase compatibility with other text manipulation programs and methods
three additional comment characters are valid if used at the beginning
of a line: &lsquo;<samp class="samp">#</samp>&rsquo;, &lsquo;<samp class="samp">|</samp>&rsquo;, and &lsquo;<samp class="samp">*</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Specifying-Amounts">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Posting-costs" accesskey="n" rel="next">Posting costs</a>, Previous: <a href="#Comments-and-meta_002ddata" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Comments and meta-data</a>, Up: <a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Journal File Format for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Specifying-Amounts-1">14.2.2 Specifying Amounts</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-amounts"></a>

<p>The heart of a journal is the amounts it records, and this fact is
reflected in the diversity of amount expressions allowed.  All of them
are covered here, though it must be said that sometimes, there are
multiple ways to achieve a desired result.
</p>
<p><em class="emph">Note:</em> It is important to note that there must be at least two
spaces between the end of the account and the beginning of the amount
(including a commodity designator).
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Integer-Amounts" accesskey="1">Integer Amounts</a></li>
<li><a href="#Commoditized-Amounts" accesskey="2">Commoditized Amounts</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Integer-Amounts">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Commoditized-Amounts" accesskey="n" rel="next">Commoditized Amounts</a>, Previous: <a href="#Specifying-Amounts" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Specifying Amounts</a>, Up: <a href="#Specifying-Amounts" accesskey="u" rel="up">Specifying Amounts</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Integer-Amounts-1">14.2.2.1 Integer Amounts</h4>

<p>In the simplest form, bare decimal numbers are accepted:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 An income transaction
    Assets:Checking        1000.00
    Income:Salary
</pre></div>

<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-uncommoditized-amounts"></a>
<p>Such amounts may only use an optional period for a decimal point.  These
are referred to as <em class="dfn">integer amounts</em> or <em class="dfn">uncommoditized
amounts</em>.  In most ways they are similar to <em class="dfn">commoditized amounts</em>,
but for one significant difference: They always display in reports with
<em class="dfn">full precision</em>.  More on this in a moment.  For now, a word must
be said about how Ledger stores numbers.
</p>
<p>Every number parsed by Ledger is stored internally as an
infinite-precision rational value.  Floating-point math is never used,
as it cannot be trusted to maintain precision of values.  So, in the
case of &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1000.00</samp>&rsquo; above, the internal value is &lsquo;<samp class="samp">100000/100</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>While rational numbers are great at not losing precision, the question
arises: How should they be displayed?  A number like &lsquo;<samp class="samp">100000/100</samp>&rsquo;
is no problem, since it represents a clean decimal fraction.  But what
about when the number &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1/1</samp>&rsquo; is divided by three?  How should one
print &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1/3</samp>&rsquo;, an infinitely repeating decimal?
</p>
<p>Ledger gets around this problem by rendering rationals into decimal at
the last possible moment, and only for display.  As such, some
rounding must, at times, occur.  If this rounding would affect the
calculation of a running total, special accommodation postings are
generated to make you aware it has happened.  In practice, it happens
rarely, but even then it does not reflect adjustment of the
<em class="emph">internal amount</em>, only the displayed amount.
</p>
<p>What has still not been answered is how Ledger rounds values.  Should
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">1/3</samp>&rsquo; be printed as &lsquo;<samp class="samp">0.33</samp>&rsquo; or &lsquo;<samp class="samp">0.33333</samp>&rsquo;?  For
commoditized amounts, the number of decimal places is decided by
observing how each commodity is used; but in the case of integer
amounts, an arbitrary factor must be chosen.  Initially, this factor
is six.  Thus, &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1/3</samp>&rsquo; is printed back as &lsquo;<samp class="samp">0.333333</samp>&rsquo;.
Further, this rounding factor becomes associated with each particular
value, and is carried through mathematical operations.  For example,
if that particular number were multiplied by itself, the decimal
precision of the result would be twelve.  Addition and subtraction do
not affect precision.
</p>
<p>Since each integer amount retains its own display precision, this is
called <em class="dfn">full precision</em>, as opposed to commoditized amounts, which
always look to their commodity to know what precision they should
round to, and so use <em class="dfn">commodity precision</em>.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Commoditized-Amounts">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Integer-Amounts" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Integer Amounts</a>, Up: <a href="#Specifying-Amounts" accesskey="u" rel="up">Specifying Amounts</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Commoditized-Amounts-1">14.2.2.2 Commoditized Amounts</h4>

<p>A <em class="dfn">commoditized amount</em> is an integer amount which has an
associated commodity.  This commodity can appear before or after the
amount, and may or may not be separated from it by a space.  Most
characters are allowed in a commodity name, except for the following:
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li>Any kind of white-space
</li><li>Numerical digits
</li><li>Punctuation: <code class="code">.,;:?!</code>
</li><li>Mathematical and logical operators: <code class="code">-+*/^&amp;|=</code>
</li><li>Bracketing characters: <code class="code">&lt;&gt;[]()</code>{}
</li><li>The at symbol: <code class="code">@</code>
</li></ul>

<p>And yet, any of these may appear in a commodity name if it is
surrounded by double quotes, for example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">100 &quot;EUN+133&quot;
</pre></div>

<p>If a <em class="dfn">quoted commodity</em> is found, it is displayed in quotes as
well, to avoid any confusion as to which part is the amount, and which
part is the commodity.
</p>
<p>Another feature of commoditized amounts is that they are reported back
in the same form as parsed.  If you specify dollar amounts using
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">$100</samp>&rsquo;, they will print the same; likewise with &lsquo;<samp class="samp">100 $</samp>&rsquo; or
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">$100.000</samp>&rsquo;.  You may even use decimal commas, such as
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">$100,00</samp>&rsquo;, or thousand-marks, as in &lsquo;<samp class="samp">$10,000.00</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>These display characteristics become associated with the commodity,
with the result being that all amounts of the same commodity are
reported consistently.  Where this is most noticeable is the
<em class="dfn">display precision</em>, which is determined by the most precise value
seen for a given commodity&mdash;in most cases.
</p>
<p>Ledger makes a distinction between <em class="dfn">observed amounts</em> and
unobserved amounts.  An observed amount is critiqued by Ledger to
determine how amounts using that commodity should be displayed;
unobserved amounts are significant in their value only&mdash;no matter how
they are specified, it does not change how other amounts in that
commodity will be displayed.
</p>
<p>An example of this is found in cost expressions, covered next.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Posting-costs">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Primary-commodities" accesskey="n" rel="next">Primary commodities</a>, Previous: <a href="#Specifying-Amounts" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Specifying Amounts</a>, Up: <a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Journal File Format for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Posting-costs-1">14.2.3 Posting costs</h4>

<p>You have seen how to specify either a commoditized or an integer
amount for a posting.  But what if the amount you paid for something
was in one commodity, and the amount received was another?  There are
two main ways to express this:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 Farmer's Market
    Assets:My Larder           100 apples
    Assets:Checking                -$20.00
</pre></div>

<p>In this example, you have paid twenty dollars for one hundred apples.
The cost to you is twenty cents per apple, and Ledger calculates this
implied cost for you.  You can also make the cost explicit using a
<em class="dfn">cost amount</em>:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 Farmer's Market
    Assets:My Larder           100 apples @ $0.200000
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>Here the <em class="dfn">per-unit cost</em> is given explicitly in the form of a cost
amount; and since cost amounts are <em class="emph">unobserved</em>, the use of six
decimal places has no effect on how dollar amounts are displayed in
the final report.  You can also specify the <em class="dfn">total cost</em>:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 Farmer's Market
    Assets:My Larder           100 apples @@ $20
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>These three forms have identical meaning.  In most cases the first is
preferred, but the second two are necessary when more than two
postings are involved:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 Farmer's Market
    Assets:My Larder           100 apples        @ $0.200000
    Assets:My Larder           100 pineapples    @ $0.33
    Assets:My Larder           100 &quot;crab apples&quot; @ $0.04
    Assets:Checking
</pre></div>

<p>Here the implied cost is &lsquo;<samp class="samp">$57.00</samp>&rsquo;, which is entered into the null
posting automatically so that the transaction balances.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Primary-commodities">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Posting-costs" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Posting costs</a>, Up: <a href="#Journal-File-Format-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Journal File Format for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Primary-commodities-1">14.2.4 Primary commodities</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dmarket-7"></a>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-_002d_002dbasis-4"></a>

<p>In every transaction involving more than one commodity, there is
always one which is the <em class="dfn">primary commodity</em>.  This commodity
should be thought of as the exchange commodity, or the commodity used
to buy and sell units of the other commodity.  In the fruit examples
above, dollars are the primary commodity.  This is decided by Ledger
based on the placement of the commodity in the transaction:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2010/05/31 Sample Transaction
    Expenses               100 secondary
    Assets                  -50 primary

2010/05/31 Sample Transaction
    Expenses               100 secondary @ 0.5 primary
    Assets

2010/05/31 Sample Transaction
    Expenses               100 secondary @@ 50 primary
    Assets
</pre></div>

<p>The only case where knowledge of primary versus secondary comes into
play is in reports that use the <samp class="option">--market (-V)</samp> or
<samp class="option">--basis (-B)</samp> options.  With these, only primary commodities are
shown.
</p>
<p>If a transaction uses only one commodity, this commodity is also
considered a primary.  In fact, when Ledger goes about ensuring that
all transactions balance to zero, it only ever asks this of primary
commodities.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>

<h4 class="subsection" id="echo-1">14.3.1 <code class="command">echo</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-echo"></a>

<p>This command simply echoes its argument back to the output.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="reload">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#source" accesskey="n" rel="next"><code class="command">source</code></a>, Previous: <a href="#echo" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><code class="command">echo</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Developer-Commands" accesskey="u" rel="up">Developer Commands</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="reload-1">14.3.2 <code class="command">reload</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-reload"></a>

<p>Forces ledger to reload any journal files.  This function exists to
support external programs controlling a running ledger process and does
nothing for a command-line user.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="source">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Debug-Options" accesskey="n" rel="next">Debug Options</a>, Previous: <a href="#reload" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><code class="command">reload</code></a>, Up: <a href="#Developer-Commands" accesskey="u" rel="up">Developer Commands</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="source-1">14.3.3 <code class="command">source</code></h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-source"></a>

<p>The <code class="command">source</code> command takes a journal file as an argument and
parses it checking for errors; no other reports are generated, and no
other arguments are necessary.  Ledger will return success if no errors
are found.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Debug-Options">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>

<h4 class="subsection" id="Debug-Options-1">14.3.4 Debug Options</h4>

<p>These options are primarily for Ledger developers, but may be of some
use to a user trying something new.
</p>
<dl class="ftable">
<dt id='index-_002d_002dargs_002donly-1'><span><samp class="option">--args-only</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dargs_002donly-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Ignore init files and environment variables for the ledger run.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002ddebug-CODE-1'><span><samp class="option">--debug <var class="var">CODE</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002ddebug-CODE-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>If Ledger has been built with debug options this will provide extra
data during the run.  Listed below are the available <var class="var">CODES</var> to
debug. You can provide multiple using a regex expression like
&quot;<code class="code">(account.display|expr.calc)</code>&quot;.
</p>
<table class="multitable">

<p>&nbsp;</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dtrace-INT-1'><span><samp class="option">--trace <var class="var">INT</var></samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dtrace-INT-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Enable tracing.  The <var class="var">INT</var> specifies the level of trace desired:
</p>
<table class="multitable">
<tbody><tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_OFF</code></td><td width="70%">0</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_CRIT</code></td><td width="70%">1</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_FATAL</code></td><td width="70%">2</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_ASSERT</code></td><td width="70%">3</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_ERROR</code></td><td width="70%">4</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_VERIFY</code></td><td width="70%">5</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_WARN</code></td><td width="70%">6</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_INFO</code></td><td width="70%">7</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_EXCEPT</code></td><td width="70%">8</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_DEBUG</code></td><td width="70%">9</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_TRACE</code></td><td width="70%">10</td></tr>
<tr><td width="30%"><code class="code">LOG_ALL</code></td><td width="70%">11</td></tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dverbose-1'><span><samp class="option">--verbose</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dverbose-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-_002dv-1'><span><samp class="option">-v</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002dv-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print detailed information on the execution of Ledger.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dverify-1'><span><samp class="option">--verify</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dverify-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Enable additional assertions during run-time.  This causes a significant
slowdown.  When combined with <samp class="option">--debug <var class="var">CODE</var></samp> ledger will
produce memory trace information.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dverify_002dmemory-1'><span><samp class="option">--verify-memory</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dverify_002dmemory-1'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Verify that every constructed object is properly destructed.  This is for
debugging purposes only.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-_002d_002dversion-3'><span><samp class="option">--version</samp><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-_002d_002dversion-3'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print version information and exit.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Pre_002dCommands">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Debug-Options" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Debug Options</a>, Up: <a href="#Developer-Commands" accesskey="u" rel="up">Developer Commands</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Pre_002dCommands-1">14.3.5 Pre-Commands</h4>
<a class="index-entry-id" id="index-pre_002dcommands"></a>

<p>Pre-commands are useful when you aren&rsquo;t sure how a command or option
will work.  The difference between a pre-command and a regular command
is that pre-commands ignore the journal data file completely, nor is
the user&rsquo;s init file read.
</p>
<dl class="ftable">
<dt id='index-eval-VEXPR'><span><code class="command">eval <var class="var">VEXPR</var></code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-eval-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Evaluate the given value expression against the model transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-format-FORMAT_005fSTRING'><span><code class="command">format <var class="var">FORMAT_STRING</var></code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-format-FORMAT_005fSTRING'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print details of how ledger uses the given formatting description and
apply it against a model transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-generate'><span><code class="command">generate</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-generate'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Randomly generates syntactically valid Ledger data from a seed.  Used
by the &lsquo;<samp class="samp">GenerateTests</samp>&rsquo; harness for development testing.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-parse-VEXPR'><span><code class="command">parse <var class="var">VEXPR</var></code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-parse-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-expr-VEXPR'><span><code class="command">expr <var class="var">VEXPR</var></code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-expr-VEXPR'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Print details of how ledger uses the given value expression description
and apply it against a model transaction.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-period-PERIOD_005fEXPRESSION'><span><code class="command">period <var class="var">PERIOD_EXPRESSION</var></code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-period-PERIOD_005fEXPRESSION'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Evaluate the given period and report how Ledger interprets it:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger period &quot;this year&quot;  --now 2011-01-01
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">--- Period expression tokens ---
TOK_THIS: this
TOK_YEAR: year
END_REACHED: &lt;EOF&gt;

--- Before stabilization ---
   range: in year 2011

--- After stabilization ---
   range: in year 2011
   start: 11-Jan-01
  finish: 12-Jan-01

--- Sample dates in range (max. 20) ---
 1: 11-Jan-01
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-query'><span><code class="command">query</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-query'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dt id='index-args'><span><code class="command">args</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-args'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Evaluate the given arguments and report how Ledger interprets it against
the following model transaction:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger query &quot;/Book/&quot;
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">--- Input arguments ---
(&quot;/Book/&quot;)

--- Context is first posting of the following transaction ---
2004/05/27 Book Store
    ; This note applies to all postings. :SecondTag:
    Expenses:Books                 20 BOOK @ $10
    ; Metadata: Some Value
    ; Typed:: $100 + $200
    ; :ExampleTag:
    ; Here follows a note describing the posting.
    Liabilities:MasterCard        $-200.00

--- Input expression ---
(account =~ /Book/)

--- Text as parsed ---
(account =~ /Book/)

--- Expression tree ---
0x7fd639c0da40    O_MATCH (1)
0x7fd639c10170     IDENT: account (1)
0x7fd639c10780     VALUE: /Book/ (1)

--- Compiled tree ---
0x7fd639c10520    O_MATCH (1)
0x7fd639c0d6c0     IDENT: account (1)
0x7fd639c0d680      FUNCTION (1)
0x7fd639c10780     VALUE: /Book/ (1)

--- Calculated value ---
true
</pre></div>

</dd>
<dt id='index-script'><span><code class="command">script</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-script'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p><small class="sc">UNDOCUMENTED</small>! Please help by contributing documentation for this feature.
</p>
</dd>
<dt id='index-template'><span><code class="command">template</code><a class="copiable-link" href='#index-template'> &para;</a></span></dt>
<dd><p>Shows the insertion template that the <code class="command">xact</code> sub-command
generates.  This is a debugging command.
</p>
</dd>
</dl>

<hr>
</div>

<div class="section-level-extent" id="Ledger-Development-Environment">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Developer-Commands" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Developer Commands</a>, Up: <a href="#Ledger-for-Developers" accesskey="u" rel="up">Ledger for Developers</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h3 class="section" id="Ledger-Development-Environment-1">14.4 Ledger Development Environment</h3>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#acprep-build-configuration-tool" accesskey="1"><samp class="file">acprep</samp> build configuration tool</a></li>
<li><a href="#Testing-Framework" accesskey="2">Testing Framework</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="acprep-build-configuration-tool">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Testing-Framework" accesskey="n" rel="next">Testing Framework</a>, Previous: <a href="#Ledger-Development-Environment" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Ledger Development Environment</a>, Up: <a href="#Ledger-Development-Environment" accesskey="u" rel="up">Ledger Development Environment</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="acprep-build-configuration-tool-1">14.4.1 <samp class="file">acprep</samp> build configuration tool</h4>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Testing-Framework">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#acprep-build-configuration-tool" accesskey="p" rel="prev"><samp class="file">acprep</samp> build configuration tool</a>, Up: <a href="#Ledger-Development-Environment" accesskey="u" rel="up">Ledger Development Environment</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Testing-Framework-1">14.4.2 Testing Framework</h4>

<p>Ledger source ships with a fairly complete set of tests to verify that
all is well, and no old errors have resurfaced.  Tests are run
individually with <samp class="file">ctest</samp>.  All tests can be run using <code class="code">make
check</code> or <code class="code">ninja check</code> depending on which build tool you prefer.
</p>
<p>Once built, the ledger executable resides under the <samp class="file">build</samp>
subdirectory in the source tree.  Tests are built and stored in the
<samp class="file">test</samp> subdirectory for the build.  For example,
<samp class="file">~/ledger/build/ledger/opt/test</samp>.
</p>

<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Running-Tests" accesskey="1">Running Tests</a></li>
<li><a href="#Writing-Tests" accesskey="2">Writing Tests</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Running-Tests">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Writing-Tests" accesskey="n" rel="next">Writing Tests</a>, Previous: <a href="#Testing-Framework" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Testing Framework</a>, Up: <a href="#Testing-Framework" accesskey="u" rel="up">Testing Framework</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Running-Tests-1">14.4.2.1 Running Tests</h4>

<p>The complete test suite can be run from the build directory using the
check option for the build tool you use.  For example, <code class="code">make
check</code>.  The entire test suit lasts around a minute for the optimized
built and many times longer for the debug version.  While developing
and debugging, running individual tests can save a great deal of time.
</p>
<p>Individual tests can be run from the <samp class="file">test</samp> subdirectory of the
build location.  To execute a single test use <code class="code">ctest -V -R regex</code>,
where the regex matches the name of the test you want to build.
</p>
<p>There are nearly 300 tests stored under the <samp class="file">test</samp> subdirectory
in the main source distribution.  They are broken into two broad
categories, baseline and regression.  To run the <samp class="file">5FBF2ED8</samp> test,
for example, issue <code class="code">ctest -V -R &quot;5FB&quot;</code>.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsubsection-level-extent" id="Writing-Tests">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Running-Tests" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Running Tests</a>, Up: <a href="#Testing-Framework" accesskey="u" rel="up">Testing Framework</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsubsection" id="Writing-Tests-1">14.4.2.2 Writing Tests</h4>

<p>To write a new test first decide to which broad category the test belongs:
baseline or regression.  Depending on the category tests are named differently
baseline tests are prefixed with their type, e.g. &lsquo;<samp class="samp">cmd</samp>&rsquo;
(see <a class="pxref" href="#Baseline-Test-Types">Baseline Test Types</a> for valid types), whereas regressions are either
named after the bug id, e.g. &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1234.test</samp>&rsquo; or uuid &lsquo;<samp class="samp">91416D62.test</samp>&rsquo;.
In case several test files belong to the same bug number the files by appending
<code class="code">_X</code> where &lsquo;<samp class="samp">X</samp>&rsquo; is the number of the test, e.g. &lsquo;<samp class="samp">1234_1.test</samp>&rsquo;,
&lsquo;<samp class="samp">1234_2.test</samp>&rsquo;.
</p>
<p>Baseline Test Types:
<a class="anchor" id="Baseline-Test-Types"></a></p><dl class="table">
<dt><code class="code">cmd</code></dt>
<dd><p>Ledger commands like <code class="command">register</code> or <code class="command">balance</code>
</p></dd>
<dt><code class="code">dir</code></dt>
<dd><p>Ledger directives like <code class="code">account</code> or <code class="code">alias</code>
</p></dd>
<dt><code class="code">feat</code></dt>
<dd><p>Ledger features such as balance assertions in journal file
</p></dd>
<dt><code class="code">opt</code></dt>
<dd><p>Ledger options such as <samp class="option">--period</samp> or <samp class="option">--format</samp>
</p></dd>
</dl>

<p>A ledger test file contains three sections:
</p>
<ol class="enumerate">
<li> the journal data used for the test, this can be empty in certain
scenarios
</li><li> the ledger command-line options used for the test
</li><li> the expected output
</li></ol>

<p>Ledger has a special command directive for tests, everything between
<code class="code">test</code> and <code class="code">end test</code> is treated like a comment, so every
Ledger test is automatically a valid Ledger file.
The test scripts take the remainder of the <code class="code">test</code> line and use
it as command-line arguments for ledger, the text enclosed in <code class="code">test</code>
and <code class="code">end test</code> is expected output, for example:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">; This is the journal data
year 2014
12/24 (C0d3) Santa Claus
  Assets:Bank         Â¤ -150,00
  Expenses:Presents

; The following line specifies the ledger command-line options for this test and
; everything between the next line and `end test` specifies the expected output
test reg --payee=code
14-Dec-24 C0d3                  Assets:Bank               Â¤ -150,00    Â¤ -150,00
14-Dec-24 C0d3                  Expenses:Presents          Â¤ 150,00            0
end test
</pre></div>

<p>When it is necessary to test for errors printed to <code class="code">stderr</code> redirect
the test output by adding <code class="code">-&gt;</code> to the <code class="code">test</code> line and match the
expected error text in an <code class="code">__ERROR__</code> section:
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">2014/01/01 * Acme Corporation
  Assets:Bank:Checking      Â¤  1.000,00
  [Fund:Vacation]           Â¤    300,00
  [Fund:Studies]            Â¤    600,00
  Income:Salary             Â¤ -2.000,00

test reg -&gt;
__ERROR__
While parsing file &quot;$FILE&quot;, line 5:
While balancing transaction from &quot;$FILE&quot;, lines 1-5:
&gt; 2014/01/01 * Acme Corporation
&gt;   Assets:Bank:Checking      Â¤  1.000,00
&gt;   [Fund:Vacation]           Â¤    300,00
&gt;   [Fund:Studies]            Â¤    600,00
&gt;   Income:Salary             Â¤ -2.000,00
Unbalanced remainder is:
           Â¤ -100,00
Amount to balance against:
          Â¤ 1.900,00
Error: Transaction does not balance
end test
</pre></div>

<p>A special <code class="code">$FILE</code> variable can be used to match the journal filename
used during the test.
</p>
<p>To add new tests to the test suite use the rebuild_cache option for the
build tool you use, for example <code class="code">make rebuild_cache</code>, now the
new tests can be run as documented in <a class="ref" href="#Running-Tests">Running Tests</a>.
</p>
<hr>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="chapter-level-extent" id="Major-Changes-from-version-2_002e6">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Example-Journal-File" accesskey="n" rel="next">Example Journal File</a>, Previous: <a href="#Ledger-for-Developers" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Ledger for Developers</a>, Up: <a href="#Top" accesskey="u" rel="up">Overview</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h2 class="chapter" id="Major-Changes-from-version-2_002e6-1">15 Major Changes from version 2.6</h2>

<p>The following have been removed from Ledger 3.0:
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li>OFX support.

</li><li>GnuCash file import.

</li><li>The option <samp class="option">--performance (-g)</samp>.

</li><li>The balance report now defaults to showing all relevant accounts.  This
is the opposite of 2.x.  That is, <code class="command">bal</code> in 3.0 does what &lsquo;<samp class="samp">-s
bal</samp>&rsquo; did in 2.x.  To see 2.6 behavior, use <samp class="option">--collapse (-n)</samp>
option in 3.0, like &lsquo;<samp class="samp">bal -n</samp>&rsquo;.  The <samp class="option">--subtotal (-s)</samp> option
no longer has any effect on balance reports.

</li></ul>

<p>The following are deprecated in Ledger 3.0:
</p>
<ul class="itemize mark-bullet">
<li>Single character value expressions are deprecated and should be changed
to the new value expressions available in 3.0

</li><li>The following environment variables have been renamed in Ledger 3.0:
<dl class="table">
<dt><code class="env">LEDGER</code></dt>
<dd><p>is now <code class="env">LEDGER_FILE</code>,
</p></dd>
<dt><code class="env">LEDGER_INIT</code></dt>
<dd><p>is now <code class="env">LEDGER_INIT_FILE</code>,
</p></dd>
<dt><code class="env">PRICE_HIST</code></dt>
<dd><p>is now <code class="env">LEDGER_PRICE_DB</code>,
</p></dd>
<dt><code class="env">PRICE_EXP</code></dt>
<dd><p>is now <code class="env">LEDGER_PRICE_EXP</code>.
</p></dd>
</dl>

</li></ul>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="appendix-level-extent" id="Example-Journal-File">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Miscellaneous-Notes" accesskey="n" rel="next">Miscellaneous Notes</a>, Previous: <a href="#Major-Changes-from-version-2_002e6" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Major Changes from version 2.6</a>, Up: <a href="#Top" accesskey="u" rel="up">Overview</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h2 class="appendix" id="Example-Journal-File-1">Appendix A Example Journal File</h2>

<p>The following journal file is included with the source distribution of
ledger.  It is called <samp class="file">drewr3.dat</samp> and exhibits many ledger
features, include automatic and virtual transactions,
</p>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">; -*- ledger -*-

= /^Income/
  (Liabilities:Tithe)                    0.12

;~ Monthly
;  Assets:Checking                     $500.00
;  Income:Salary

;~ Monthly
;   Expenses:Food  $100
;   Assets

2010/12/01 * Checking balance
  Assets:Checking                   $1,000.00
  Equity:Opening Balances

2010/12/20 * Organic Co-op
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 37.50  ; [=2011/01/01]
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 37.50  ; [=2011/02/01]
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 37.50  ; [=2011/03/01]
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 37.50  ; [=2011/04/01]
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 37.50  ; [=2011/05/01]
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 37.50  ; [=2011/06/01]
  Assets:Checking                   $ -225.00

2010/12/28=2011/01/01 Acme Mortgage
  Liabilities:Mortgage:Principal    $  200.00
  Expenses:Interest:Mortgage        $  500.00
  Expenses:Escrow                   $  300.00
  Assets:Checking                  $ -1000.00

2011/01/02 Grocery Store
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 65.00
  Assets:Checking

2011/01/05 Employer
  Assets:Checking                   $ 2000.00
  Income:Salary

2011/01/14 Bank
  ; Regular monthly savings transfer
  Assets:Savings                     $ 300.00
  Assets:Checking

2011/01/19 Grocery Store
  Expenses:Food:Groceries             $ 44.00 ; hastag: not block
  Assets:Checking

2011/01/25 Bank
  ; Transfer to cover car purchase
  Assets:Checking                  $ 5,500.00
  Assets:Savings
  ; :nobudget:

apply tag hastag: true
apply tag nestedtag: true
2011/01/25 Tom's Used Cars
  Expenses:Auto                    $ 5,500.00
  ; :nobudget:
  Assets:Checking

2011/01/27 Book Store
  Expenses:Books                       $20.00
  Liabilities:MasterCard
end tag
2011/12/01 Sale
  Assets:Checking:Business            $ 30.00
  Income:Sales
end tag
</pre></div>

<h3 class="section" id="Cookbook-1">B.1 Cookbook</h3>


<ul class="mini-toc">
<li><a href="#Invoking-Ledger" accesskey="1">Invoking Ledger</a></li>
<li><a href="#Ledger-Files" accesskey="2">Ledger Files</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Invoking-Ledger">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Next: <a href="#Ledger-Files" accesskey="n" rel="next">Ledger Files</a>, Previous: <a href="#Cookbook" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Cookbook</a>, Up: <a href="#Cookbook" accesskey="u" rel="up">Cookbook</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>
</div>
<h4 class="subsection" id="Invoking-Ledger-1">B.1.1 Invoking Ledger</h4>


<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger --group-by &quot;tag('trip')&quot; bal
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger cleared VWCU NFCU Tithe Misentry
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger register Joint --uncleared
</pre></div>
<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">$ ledger register Checking --sort d -d 'd&gt;[2011/04/01]' until 2011/05/25
</pre></div>

<hr>
</div>
<div class="subsection-level-extent" id="Ledger-Files">
<div class="nav-panel">
<p>
Previous: <a href="#Invoking-Ledger" accesskey="p" rel="prev">Invoking Ledger</a>, Up: <a href="#Cookbook" accesskey="u" rel="up">Cookbook</a> &nbsp; [<a href="#SEC_Contents" title="Table of contents" rel="contents">Contents</a>][<a href="#Concepts-Index" title="Index" rel="index">Index</a>]</p>

<h4 class="subsection" id="Ledger-Files-1">B.1.2 Ledger Files</h4>

<div class="example smallexample">
<pre class="example-preformatted">= /^Income:Taxable/
  (Liabilities:Tithe Owed)    -0.1
= /Noah/
  (Liabilities:Tithe Owed)    -0.1
= /Jonah/
  (Liabilities:Tithe Owed)    -0.1
= /Tithe/
  (Liabilities:Tithe Owed)    -1.0
</pre></div>

<hr>
<h4 class="footnotes-heading">Footnotes</h4>

<h5 class="footnote-body-heading"><a id="FOOT1" href="#DOCF1">(1)</a></h5>
<p>In some special
cases, it automatically balances this transaction for you.</p>
<h5 class="footnote-body-heading"><a id="FOOT2" href="#DOCF2">(2)</a></h5>
<p>This also means if you
misspell an account it will end up getting counted separately from
what you intended.  An Emacs major mode
<a class="uref" href="https://github.com/ledger/ledger-mode/">ledger-mode</a> provides
tab completion for automatically filling in account names.</p>
<h5 class="footnote-body-heading"><a id="FOOT3" href="#DOCF3">(3)</a></h5>
<p>You
can track <em class="emph">anything</em>, even time or distance traveled.  As long as
it cannot be created or destroyed inside your accounting system.</p>
